When solution of belly comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retentive and digestive virtues that is in stomach and in intestine are bled, and cannot be cured by manners of cures; and you see the patient well suffering and of great virtue, so make one great cautery upon the stomach according to what he has spoken before or cautery of the stomach, at the circulating cautery; and four cauteries around the subtle bud all one cautery clavil subtil, and two cauteries on the loins.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistors abundant and the patient suffering, make cautery on the dagger, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, because the cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are on the foundation, or one or more, and they are old and are large humors cold and moist corrupted, and they are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not help, if cauteries are made: three on the spine of the back, that which is all outside below the armpit point to point in a triangle, and one cautery under the buttocks two fingers;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swollen, then on the face make one large cautery on the stomach, as it has been said before, and one other on the liver, and one other on the mice to all the clavicle cautery; and leave the cautery open long time. After the cure the place as long as it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the flesh which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the "thelul," sharpen the cautery which seems like a razor, and then put it all ablaze on that "thelul" cut; and leave it there as long as the cautery comes to the base of the vein, so that the blood stops; do this once or twice, and if there is much "thelul," cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure of beneficial ointments as long as they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the flesh, it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	of a poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will recount in its place, then comes such a disease that can only be healed by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to any one and is filled and rotten with corrupted moisture, then you must first probe it thoroughly with a probe, and guard that you know the extent of the probe how much it has gone in. After cauterize the cautery which seems like a razor, and put it into the fistula according to the quantity that the probe went into, and re-begin the cautery until the corrupted flesh is burned, one time, or two, or three, according to the quantity of its need; and guard yourself from burning the nerve that are there, and the large veins. If the fistula goes towards the body of the bladder and the intestine, then guard these places, and do not make cuts except in their fleshy part, and think that it is not pierced; after cure the place as long as it is healthy, and if the place is healed, and the matters are removed long time, then know that the place is completely healed; and if the matters are not removed, know that the place is troubled, and corrupted bone at its foundation; and thus as one of these that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and of great flatulence, and does not take (medicine) for woman, then it behooves you to make a cautery upon the kidneys on one part and on the other with the cautery clavile that we have said before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in line, and they will do more help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and soft from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs begin at the groin, one on the right and one on the left, and let each cautery be as long as a finger; and you make one cautery behind the back, or two if you need it; and let the cauteries be shaped according to the form previously stated.
de la marris	of the kidneys
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the kidneys are cold and moist, and do not allow for conception because of this, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are slow to come; and when they do come, there is great pain: therefore it behooves one to make three cauteries around the waist, as we have said about the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries behind the back; and let the cauteries be shaped like a wedge, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous humors descend to the hip joint, and because of this they move out of place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the location is found in the region above the hip, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the hip joint at i. cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the place around the joint as it turns, so that the joint is inside the circle; and let the cautery be like that with which one has cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present to you, then make iij. cauteries of the olive-sized large ones, and let the cautery be as deep as all the others; and treat until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division and the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills, or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to 2 manners: that is to say together with burning medicines, and fire cautery. The fire cautery is according to many manners, of which one is such: that you cauterize on the hip joint 3 triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them good depth and large, and have between each cautery a space the size of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes it is done to cauterize in the middle on the top of the hip, for which there are 4 according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you want, cauterize with the circular cautery that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; but do in such a manner that the circle contains the whole hip, and all the spaces of the heart be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the manner in which it is done in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip, and does not reach to the thigh nor to the leg. And if it comes to the thigh and the leg, then one makes .ij. cauteries where the patient says that the pain holds him, and .i. cautery above the ankle .iiij. fingers, on the left side a point; and whether the cauteries are cutting or burned the thickness of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers of the foot or near it, then one cauterizes where he feels the pain .iij. points or .iiij. at the cautery which is called "points."
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, one makes more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then one makes a cautery with the cutting or circular cautery, and be careful in all your cauteries that you do not leave so much of the cautery that you burn the nerves and the great arteries, and that you do not make more harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who made cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left it so much that the leg was all swollen, and the foot too, and was pierced and corrupted throughout the foot. After a solution of the belly from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner. // And the sage said in the cautery of the hip, from which this is the manner, make one such iron and be at the head also thick as a hazelnut of finger, or a little less, and be between stitches and be from one stitch to another with spacing the quantity of a knuckle; and let the stitches be towards two parts, and be also like nuts, and have one hand of iron well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated until it is all red and feels hot, and then put it on the bone of the sick hip, and be turned onto the healthy side; and cauterize once one cautery return and let it leave three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open long time; after the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim said that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its regard, and it is seen little who uses it; and nonetheless those are good cauteries, which can bear it, and where it is needed.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or by percussion or by too great evacuation, or by similar appearance of cold matter spread, to none of these appearances is cautery suitable, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this, that the patient be free of foul pills or other similar things, that one makes on their back, where the pain holds, three lines marked with enche, and in each line .v. cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery which is called "poins"; and if you see it, make .iij. cauteries or .iiij. at the clavile cautery middle according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to little children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have a constricted belly when they cry, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance which comes on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you will cure it, cauterize it with the cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery pricks each part of the spine evenly. And if you see it, cauterize around the spine with the pointed cautery 2 or 3 lines, and let the points be near each other. After cure the place as long as it is healed according to what we have said, and guard that you do not bring cautery in a cavity which is in nerve spame.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of the joints are from dampness which are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, that the wise call "gout" properly, and when it is of cold cause and cures by medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make the mound of cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then you make cautery to the whole cautery as one claims "point". And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then you make cautery on each knee three or four cauteries of each part, to the whole olive cautery; and if you have need for more, then you make more, but do not hold your hand further than while the tip of the heart is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knee and the back, then administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, then make points around the socket two lines; and if there remains no pain in the arms, then make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and do good governance to the patient and pure medicines. For if you do good governance to him and you purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sciatic nerve
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture comes in the groin, and the balls descend to the thighs, and it is new, then when you see it healed, that he does not move his leg that day; and that he uses things which make the belly softer, so that the bowels descend from his belly; after that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm as long as the balls are repaired, and move them to your sides, and take a sign of a half-circle above the groin; then burn the cautery with this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and it feels hot. Then move the balls to their place; and the minister holds his hand above so that they do not return backward; and work well the thighs of the patient, and put under him one cushion and one bandage on the thighs, and one other on the leg which keeps his hands; then place the cautery on the sign with all your strength, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, restart it again until you come to the bone; and be careful that the balls do not jump when you do the cautery; that you do not burn them; and that by this the patient does not die, or other evils.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to their measure, and for big people as big according to their measure; after 3 days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the burning is removed; after that cure other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his dressings be long so that the balls do not jump when he wants to go to bed.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, a well-made bandage is given to him, and it is worn for another 40 days; and have good rest, that he does not work too much and be wary of too much drink and eating, and of too much bragging; and when he follows this teaching, he will be entirely healed. And I will say afterwards the cure of the thigh in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow anymore, to him make 1 cautery of the cautery reont according to its quantity, and be it at the third of the heart; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one should cauterize with the cautery at 3 angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But first sign the place of the inche and make a line through the width above the rupture, and another outside, and hold your hand over all the cautery clavicle. But the first cauteries are lighter and more movable.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from a fall or a blow, and this pain lasts long, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "poins", and let the cautery be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its virtue and its location of torsions and of its pain. If it is healed by the first cautery, that's good; if not, begin again with another cautery on top of it, because it is customary that it must be moved to the member that is closest to it, so it is necessary for you to make the cauteries as long as the patient is not healed.
de meselerie	of mixture
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The mixtures are aided at times by cautery with great help, and also the patient that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. As you see them cauterized, take care if the patient is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not send nor stay, and you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the patient, then make .v. cauteries on the head: .i. remove the head to nine, and the other towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; and .ij. on the .ij. horns, and .i. behind on the back of the neck; and let your hand so that the cauteries come up to the bone, and as long as the skins go out so that the vapors of the thick humors can issue; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixture is spread everywhere; and it manifests itself clearly, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said on the head, and .i. cautery in the middle of the neck, and .ij. cauteries on the spine of the neck, and .vj. cauteries on the spine of the back, and .i. great one on the hip and .i. other near the groin, and .ij. on the .ij. shoulders; and .ij. on the ribs, and .ij. on the tendons of the thigh, and .i. on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are on the lower heel, that you do not burn them; and sometimes it is done to cauterize on the bone of the arm, and .i. other on the bone of the stomach, and .i. other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And knows that when more there is made cautery, more it does help, and moves him profit; and knows that the patient feels no pain in cautery as much as the healthy ones feel it, because the body is already all corrupt. And it behoves that the cauteries be great and small according to the members and the joints, according to what you will find in manners of irons. After cure its place with flour of times with honey and other cures until it be healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes in any member and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauteries on the member according to the size and smallness of the member; and let the cautery be one point deep into the thickness of the flesh; then cure with dressings until it be healed. And sometimes one makes cautery and in the hand and in the foot and in the back, at the end of the nerve that moves the member, and thus is removed the swelling; and nevertheless do not intervene anyone unless he is knowing of the members and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of almonds
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the malady that is called "albaras" is enfeebling, and the means of medicine are of no avail, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of the species of heart, until the white part is removed and its color is changed; then cure it with flour of beans and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood from the colon and blood from the alondre, each one part; and mix all together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of syphilis by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When syphilis appears at the beginning, and you see it arrested, then cauterize it with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the chancre. And nonetheless, the wise ones say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; and nonetheless this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never seen it happen before. And the more right thing is that it be cauterized around, with a cautery that is called "circule," as we have said in much of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati," and it takes a long time to heal, or because of the superfluity that it makes, or because of the blood of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the tension; and you see it hasten to heal: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries by pricking; after which leave it as it is. For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it becoming worse with the whole cautery, then heat the cautery with this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" as long as the cautery pierces the core, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it burning from within in such a way that the course of the rot is alleviated. Afterward, care for it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	There is another way of illness which is called "corroding", and it is nothing else but a gangrene of the limb, because it rots the limbs just like fire rots dry wood. If you see this disease in someone who can endure cauterization with fire, then burn small and large cauteries on them, according to what is fitting for the place where the disease is; after which cauterize all sides until you remove all corruption, so that nothing of it remains, that all that is corrupted is removed. And then let it be for 3 days, and put over the cauterized places a softened broil with oil until the scabs of fire are removed, and all the corruption. Then after the cure of healing-bringing flesh. And if you see after 3 days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, then begin again the cautery on what remains corrupted.  And this gangrene has been cured sometimes with a medicine of water in place of fire cauterization; but nonetheless, fire cauterization is more helpful, and I have already said the cure of the water medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	from the roots that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that the feet by fire are born a sickness which is called «clos» according to our understanding, and it is a large thing that spoils the foot. And the cauteries of this sickness are so in .ij. ways. That is to say cautery of fire, and cautery of hot water. The cautery of fire so is that you heat .i. cautery cheveit as it is a feather of vulture, and be made of good iron to the measure that it can hold the nail from all sides, and that it have subtle edges; after that put all hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and let him so .iij. days until it begins to give rot; then I do a plaster of wild malves ground with seil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nails will fall and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with ointment enclosing flesh as much as is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by fire the body, and many times happens in hands and feet, then it is necessary that you bring them cautery of hot water; and is in such a manner: take a chain of iron or iron, or a feather of vulture, and put on the nail and the other one, that is to say porrelz warts; and put the chain so that it holds all around, then put a pot of hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the chain comes to the root of the nail, and may find the hot water way deep to the root; and suffer the patient a while the biting of the hot water an hour; then let him, and he will be uprooted at all his roots. Thus do one after another, as long as you eradicate all those that are in the body, then cure them with ointments that enclose flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold or from quartan fever or another, it is fitting that you make to them four cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery or weight, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; so will he stop trembling, and hasten the health from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	of suppurating pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes pustules appear on the body bathed in fire, or suppurating pustules, that come from large corrupted matters. Thus it is fitting at first when they appear that one make cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle stick, so that its point be seized by fire, or of long arnica root, or at the lentil-shaped cautery. And sometimes the cauterize them at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further in advance, but are disrupted the superfluities from which they come, and are healed; but it is fitting that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great hemorrhages from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the outside, or in the incision of an abscess, or to the cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is very grievous thing to be prolonged.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, hasten to place your finger index upon the wound of the vein, and restrain it very much until the blood is appeased under your finger, and no more drops out; then put on fire the olive cauteries more small and great as many as they are red; then grasp i., or large or small according to the wound and its place where the artery is routed, and put the cautery upon that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery as long as the bleeding is restrained.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it leaps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily i. other of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to make them one after the other until the vein is stretched; and watch that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the patient; and know that when a vein runs out of the artery, it cannot be well stretched even if the artery is large, unless by one of the four ways that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong tying of a thread, or by medicines put upon which have power to stretch blood; and let it be bound and constrained firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring the tightening of linen or straps tightly or putting burning things on, or similar things, if it does not benefit, no.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has no medicine present, then he must put his finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and tighten it well until it is stretched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but moisten the hand with cold water often that it be very cold until the blood is frozen and thickened and stretched; and make those in advance which he needs for cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures of tail
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery, or burning medicine, and their incisions, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I placed that chapter from head to foot, and I will go in this chapter by the same way for those who find it more easily what they want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, since I begin this one, it is necessary, dear friend, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauteries, and for this reason, greater caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly.  For many kinds of people come to cures. They come from those who are so weakened by their illness that they die easily because of the ignorance they find in their disease, and of the greatness of their malice; and of these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these there are those who give their sense, and say: “Wait, I am cured”; and the disease is spiteful. It does not become you that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not operate foolishly but wisely of those whom you are certain of, and whom you can have taken and praise; and use prognosis and indication in cures of your patients so that health be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of long.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, May our Lords give you good understanding and uprightness, and if you will aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered you this chapter by chapters, according to that which it is before or chapter of cauteries, that I have devised from the head to the feet, for those that you find more easily those of which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes many times to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls the head of the child too hard; and some times it comes from a cause unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness outside of children, and to all those that I have seen it has hastened death; and for this reason it seems to me that it is better to leave the work in such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the head grew larger each day until it could not be supported; and so much moisture accumulated that he died, and this moisture is assembled under the bone on the scapula, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such when the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you cut in the middle of the head a wide opening; and let it be as long as two fingers, as far as the moisture goes; and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more deep, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the manner of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the sutures of the head open on each side, and the water leaps out when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not return to you: then it is necessary that you cut in the middle of the head three incisions according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision extract the moisture entirely outwards. After extract the slits of drapes and powders, and put there wine and oil, and leave thus until the fifth day; then untie it, and cure the wound by tents and ointments, and let the chief bandage remain tightened, and then feed the patient dry meat from a little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look where opens the greatness of the abscess, and its assembly of water; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore cut where the abscess opens, and its filling of water, and open it according to what you have power; and beware that you do not sever the artery; and vein flow of blood, so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to any one a malady that is called «catarre» in the eyes or at the breast, and the illness is old, and the cure of medicine does not help, then the last cure is the cautery with those one covers the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, when you see to cover them, that the patient make his head back; after rub their place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then restrain the patient his neck with one cloth; then look where the vein beats, and the places of one and the other are after the ears, and so they are placed; then sign the places of each, then cut both with an acute spatula of two parts. As long as the incision reaches to the bone, and this is by the wide side of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, plunge the spatula below the artery and cut it above, cutting also as two fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood jumps out from above continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open at the touch, you must measure the space of three fingers, then seize and cut up to the bone; and that which it is necessary to let out blood is six finger widths, and perhaps one more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the fullness of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone point without a sign of pus, cut it so that an abscess does not come there, then restrain the wound and tie it, and care with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	Of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes, and acute catarrh, for the moistures of tears and the heats in the temples and ancient foreskin and similar things, and it is medicated by means of cures of medicine and all those do not benefit it, then we drain the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of their extraction is that the patient make rear the hairs of his temples, and attend to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is poorly returned outside than in some men who are too cold; and if it is returned, it is strained its neck the patient from some cloths, then rubs the place with some rough cloth, and rose the place of hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then scrape the skin lightly until you come to the artery, then pull it up as pincers, and depart well from the tissues that are under each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it to the point of the forceps, then cut it off from that side according to the quantity of .ij. fingerbreadths. For if it is not cut, it does not jump out entirely at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from .vj.  c/ to .iij.; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in .ij. lengths with a strong double thread of silk, so that putrefaction does not come before the sewing of the wound, and there comes bleeding; then cut the superfluity which is between the .ij. ligatures in the same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with the cupped cautery up to the bone until the fingerbreadths are cut; and this is the best work, if the patient has no fever and he is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is aid to finish the moisture: for this reason it is of greater help against the moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fill their place with old cotton and put tents well made on top; and when they are untied, be careful to use dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and tents, until it is healed; and if without a piece of the artery as much as you work on it, then hurry to cover it with cautery, or you put the place of vitriol and strain it in your hand that the blood stops; and if you don't have those present, put on the place your thumb until the bleeding ceases, and raise the place of cold water until the bleeding stops, and be strained as is necessary; and what is most effective and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery trenchant of .ij. parts, but let the trenches be well spaced to hold their heat for longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too thick, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two knives one that is a good thickness, and then when you have signed in the two sides, and you put the red hot iron over until it comes to the bone, and cut the vein in two fingers; and be separated between the two shoulders because it is not joined of this cautery at all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are on the top of the head of fur, and it does not profit any cure of medicine is done, and you see the face of the patient encircle, and feels on the forehead walk like of a trembling; and where oil are wet and moist so that the hair of the papers are falling, and are dried out the papers, and scorched by the ardor of the tears, so it needs this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called it in the old days "contused cure," and it is that you do behind to the patient who has this sickness the hairs that he have or front, then him make .iij. cuts or front equally according to the length of the front; and let one of the cuts be as .ii. doing all the way through the front in going down until the nose, and the others .ii. at .ii. ribs above the ears, and guard yourself from the incision of the arteries that are at the .ii. ribs above the ears; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the .ii. mandibles, and let each wound be the quantity of .iij. fingers across joined;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and much of cloths its for to wipe the blood, then put the spatula sharp of .ii. parts from that which is here the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is over the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the marrow that is between the .ii. cuts at all the fascia that is above the bone, then make another from the middle incision until the other second, and then extract further this spatula
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If put in the first fissure the instrument that is called "cultellaire", and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put the sharp side towards the flesh towards the heart, and the blunt side towards the bone, and thrust it until it reaches the middle fissure. And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as long as the incision is continuous up to that which opens near the heart, and then on the other side make in the middle fissure up to the other opening; and then extract the blood evenly, and express the wound for the drawn blood; then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put above cloths moistened in wine and oil and asiel, and guard that abscesses do not come there; and on the third day untie the linen, and then administer a great quantity of tepid water, then the cure of basil ointment with rose oil, and other cures as for curing wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eye's
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to any come a sharp catarrh, and you see the eyes watery and small, and weakening of sight, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and where chief in them make an acute pain, and the patient sneezes; therefore know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh do not come but from many veins, and the moisture cure that is there, so is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And is that you command the patient to rear his forehead, then make a great gash between the brow, and another wide one.  i.e. poc. And begin from the fissure of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move in the mouth; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then sew between the .ij. edges of the gash and put old cotton there, and linen bandages; then tie above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and keep yourself away from a hot abscess; when it is removed, you must rub the bone as long as char begins to rise, then cure it with drying things that make char begin to harden.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take .ij. parts of wheat flower, and .iiij. parts of colophony, and make a plaster from them; and administer it in these wounds to cause char to grow throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which falls into the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or stone of mine or similar thing as iron; or seed, as beans, lentils, peas; or flowing thing as water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When something falls into the ear, a stone or another manner of thing that does not join to the ear nor grow in the ear, put the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, distill any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze with condiment, and stop his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear upwards. Often it comes forth by this cure; and if it does not come forth, administer extraction with fine pincers, for this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps forth with the pincers, that is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine instrument of small doubleure; and if it does not jump forth by this, make a chain of iron and put the head of the chain or through the opening of the ear forcefully, and stop what is around the chain with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the chain; then pull forth forcefully, for often it comes forth as we have said; and if it does not come forth in this manner, take a gut which they use to catch birds, and put into some instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a bit of cotton around; then press the gut on the stone or whatever it may be, and pull forth.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not follow all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut open the ear so as an abscess comes out, and spasms; and the manner of cutting it is that you first make the patient healthy in the head, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and making a small cut at the root of the ear to the fat or where it depends; and let the cut be like a moon, as far as you come to the stone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it gently with your mouth; and the care until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot issue, then administer i. spatula tenve subtle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer incision of that grain. But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist for the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract with subtle pincers and by suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the ear when water falls, it is appropriate for the patient to use a first-aid of a compress and open the ear with old cotton. And let him lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out by this, it is good. If it doesn't come out, take many pebbles according to the length of your finger, light and easy, and heat them a little in the fire; and put them in the patient’s one pierced ear, and put on top of it from the other side, and place another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and don't stop doing this of stone by stone until all the water comes out, and so it will come out entirely.
