And if you see it, take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end catch fire until the tip of the reed burns; then redo another with other reeds until the water is entirely gone, as we have said before with the pebbles.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small-bodied, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large-bodied that one can feel it, administer an extraction with tweezers; and it is the lightest thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and where we treated distillations, and the cure does not benefit, it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, then treat them with fine tweezers, and if they don't appear, take the dog of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And let it be narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle chief in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed them throughout the entire caine; do this often as long as all the worms come out.  And if they do not obey to come out, then stuff around the caine with cotton as I said in the piere; and if they do not come out further as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the excision of worms, and you will find them treating distillations; and if you distill your oils and your medicines in the ear to all this instrument, for this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be of silver or of iron, narrow below with i. small holes, and wide above to distill; and for pressing inside the distillation i. instrument of iron well made for this, and if you see take i. razor and wrap around the tip conveniently cotton; then put your oil or your juice, and what you see of your medicines in the caine, and let the caine be in the ear; then put inside the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or at the end of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillations be i. pock heated at the fire as it is distilled in the ear; and guard that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men through the clogging of a wound, or flesh growing inside the ear, and these blockages come sometimes from within the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes there are i.e., a poke of pus, and it can be seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes from within, if one cannot see it, is of great harm in many dispositions, and in this case you should put the ear of the sick person to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening apparent, then the work has all these spatumiles of which this is the form.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and trenchant before and behind all plain, so that it does not blister the ear; if the opening is of flesh growing or a piece of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut it lightly, until that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the suppuration is in the ear, take one razor subtle and light and heat it a little at the fire, then put it into the body of the ear. If you feel the suppuration that the patient feels great pain in the ear, pierce lightly, and keep that you do not wound the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the opening, and moisten it in the Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this with no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on powdered vitriol; and if you see swelling in the ear, then it is necessary that you withdraw the tent and move another tent moistened in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, then dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the bleeding which are or treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the sheet of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althule that comes on papers of the eyes when they are moist and are dry, it behooves you to extend them with pliers and tweezers, and the edge of a spatula from their roots; then put on their place powdered vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it decorates, then cauterize with a fine lentil cautery, and the cauterization after the incision is worth moves; and many times they return, since nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gristle
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come in papers the eyes some things that seem brittle in its form and in its hardness, and for this reason is this disease called "hail", and is an assembly of moisture thick in the paper above and below; the work is such: take care if the hail moves from one part and another, and this is a light thing to know; then make the large, then the scrape of each part lightly, then take it with pliers, and cut. If you cannot cut it without piercing a little the paper, so it grieves nothing to the sick; and if the fissure is great, so the assemble with a suture, and the cure until it is healed; and if it is small, so make no force, for the ointment restores it quickly and prevents flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending down into the ear towards the upper part, so turn the paper, and being the hail to pliers, and cut it and press from one side and another; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it grieves nothing; and when the hail is cut, so leave the eye of salted water, and cure the place with that which prevents flesh until the sick be healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	This is grease that is created in the webs of the papers above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it grieves much their eyes, and they come the catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces afterwards, and sleep on them, and are their papers under their eyebrows moist that the swelling and the appearance have covered with the exinach which opens in the eye. And when you press its place with your fingers and feel the exirnach between.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on your shoulder; and then take one drapeil of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exirnach from each part, then put it on top of him; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exirnach is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with the sharp spatula a fissure of a width, and not be more than the wound made in the vein; and make the skin in length as far as you come to the exirnach; and in more places comes exirnach from the fissure, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then a whole piece of cloth with your fingers at the outside, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread; and guard that you do not add in the fissure, that you come to the entire spatula up to the eye, that you do not blind him.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exirnach does not open at the beginning of the fissure, so accroi a little the fissure lightly until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then moisten bandages in aisil and in water, and put on top, and strain with bands.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it happens to such men who grind the herb and put on top to corrupt that moisture which is stayed. Then cure it until it is healed. And if it comes to the place a hot abscess, then cure with ointments soothing until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs grow arranged other than the natural ones, and are inflamed, they harm the eyes and bring many kinds of maladies as accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albuginea, as much as that is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to .iiij. manners: or by cautery altogether fire, or by medicine ague according to this that it is before or chapter of cautery, and it is made or by incision and stitch or by caines, according to that which I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It behooves you to put the head of the patient in your healthy one, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if this is not so, there puts an needle to all .i. thread above; and let it be below the margin of the paper or where the hair grows next to these hairs, and trace .i. thread upward to the entire paper, and turn it back to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs arranged, to all the spatula cutting, from the large tear to the small one; then extract .i. thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then reign above the paper a figure of an enche, as the leaf of myrtle, and however it behooves that the figure is according to the quantity that you see raise the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if to that one who needs it, then cut a great quantity of the paper according to this that the paper is softened; then make at all the spatula above the .ij. lines that you have signed, and begin from the large tear to the small one; and let be one of the slits near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the needle in one of the .ij. angles of the heart, then scrape it completely; then assemble the .ij. lips with a stitch of a needle with all .i. thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make air to the superfluity of the threads on the .ij. eyebrows to any glues things, if you want to do this; and if not, have no care about it, then leave the stitch and the threads up to .iij. days or .iiij.; then cure the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, for the paper revives by the healing of the wound and the assembling of it, but the stitch is muddled (as the ancients said), and this work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if in another manner: and it is that you draw the paper of a figure which is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have counted, at three inches wide according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut that which rises above the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have power to hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle which has one thread, and put it in the middle of the figure; and put one other thread along the large tear, and the second thread along the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above where you have drawn, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then appease it with cerote and similar soothing ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: so it is necessary that you use those that we have said of the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the splints is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the felt inside according to those that I have said, and then make .ij. splints by art, and .ij. subtle ligaments as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and cut the .ij. heads of .ij. parts where you hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other subtly on top of that which overhangs the paper of the eye, and strain the .ij. splints of the .ij. parts form; and let it remain thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and wrinkle and carry itself, until it falls by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it tarries, if it is cut with more force, then the cure as long as it is healthy; and when the wound is healed, and if the paper is raised, and they will no longer prick the hairs; and this is the form of the .ij. splints that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works is such that you prick a subtle needle, and put in it one thread of silk, soft and subtle; then assemble the heads and knot them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then order in the chase another thread of silk, finely braided, and knot the chief of the threads; then put the patient’s head on your healthy one; and let it be in the sun so that the work is clarified, for it is a subtle and fine work, then put the needle all the way into the chase in the root of the hair adjacent, and make it pierce in the paper carefully until you draw it from above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put in the chase that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then extract your hand so that the hairs come out all the way into the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will draw the chase down to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes out of the opening above and you see it with the vision of your eye; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair is rooted in its place and grows the flesh above; and if the hair is small, accompany it with one long hair from the natural ones, and let it be raised with that one or you leave it, until it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this sickness which is called 'aleacrati' or rot comes in the eye, if there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.  And happens by suddenness of wound, or cutting, or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of operating in it is that you split the suture and separate its lips, and put inside tents of linen, and let it be until it is healed; and it is not fitting that you use in the cure of it things that dry and restrain. For if you do this, then the sickness returns worse than at first; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and the rose of water or althea and flaxseed are cooked, and the diaquilon ointment melted into any of the oils, and envelop a tent, and cure it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not suture according to the form that it was before; and these operations that we have said are nothing but remedies for this sickness, that it may not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the char that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is desoz which truly is called “axacrati”, and is natural and accidental. The accidents come from wound and fissure and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you prick an needle, in which there are .i. double thread, and stick it in the char, and make it go from the left tear to the right, so that the threads come in .ij. chiés of the char; then keep the char above the whole needle, and cut at .i. spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper comes back according to what it ought, it is good; if those are not, then take .i. razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make .ij. fissures or cuts inside the paper; and let the chiés of the .ij. fissures be at the .ij. angles of the incision that you have cut, and make two angles so that when they are assembled, the figure is as the figure of a letter which has the name “."j. griesche"; then remove that char, according to the quantity that its costs are augmented below, from those who follow the paper, then adjust the .ij. parts separated, and sew them with a thread of linen; then cure with what we have said about softening medicines, and bandages, as long as it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the ailment comes from a split or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you split a plain cut under the hairs of the papers, and according to what has been said before; then sever between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the malady, because it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters equip everything with all their power how it makes return the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is necessary for the operation and instruments in more dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper's
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this soldering happens to a man's eye in such a manner that the paper above is soldered with the white of the egg, and cannot move nor perform its natural workings, then it is necessary that you put the tip of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and the being as pinches, until you cut what is attached to the spatula fine, which must not be too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient may not suffer that the spatula too sharp or bleaches the eye; and let your incision, with which you remove this assembly, be gentle, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and it is healed all of this assembly, and one does no time in the eye salty water, and the leavings of fresh water, and of coliere; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened in the white of an egg; and after the third day use the coliere and the things soudans until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is in two ways: it is nervouse and similar to one hard syfac, and another which is not nervouse, but is similar to white moisture congealed, that when one touches it with iron and one boils it panre as pinches, so one cannot; and the one and the other semblance begins towards the great tear, and crosses poc and poc until it covers all the view and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then opens his eyes; and lift the paper with your hand, then coil the angle as pinches of small doubleure, and the rest upwards; then take a needle, and put on it one hair of horse, or of calf, or of ox, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle a poc and put it in the angle, and pierce it with all the needle, and tie the angle with a thread and the rest upwards, and scar the whole hair along the side of the angle which follows the prunele and silk to the hair up to the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear with all the spatumile subtle and small forces, and leave the char natureil or tear, so that by the incision does not come the body of tears acostumeement; and no times is it ascended the angle only, and on the thread, as we have said; then the scar on all the spatumile souef of this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the needle is not pierced; and after the incision put in the eye a bit of silk ground, and from the collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then cure it as much as it needs until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot put the needle in, and the tweezers cannot enter, many times this kind of nail is cured with medicines; and it grows as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, it works the eye of the patient, and take the spatula lightly pointed according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail carefully, and if you see that it does not lessen and the reason hastens, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red ochre and ground silk, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is against you in the eye, like an abscess, then milk it, and treat the abscess first as hot as long as it is healed, then restart the work as before, as long as it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear hurts in the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it to the armpit and cut a part and not half altogether, so that no body of tears comes; then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The eyes of some men are born at times with red flesh, and it covers the iris and restrains itself on the eyelids and turns them outward, and seems like a rose of bloom; and the work for this is that the patient puts his head in your health, then works the eyes, and coils all that flesh with suitable tweezers to this, and supports it with force; then cut the first flesh, and go cutting all the way down to the end, and keep yourself that you don't wound the eye during the work; and let the incision of the spatula be as we have said in the incision of the angle and small forces of which one removes the sebum, as how it demonstrates after this chapter the form;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of seal ground or distill there red mercury and similar corrosive medicines, and put on top of the oil boiled cotton with egg white, so that it may be sure of a hot abscess; and if it remains nothing, and the without cloth covering is mounted, and you doubt hot abscess, then leave the oil and cure the abscess with things soothing hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do as long as flesh is attached in the eye by this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless it is necessary that you apply the cure of each weak oil by nature's way; and of the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member be suffering from this work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Blood vessels are red that cover the eye, and take away from the view their work and weaken the eye all days. It is necessary then that you first look at the eye, in which it is, whether it is, or not, and there is no other illness besides the blood vessel; therefore, the coil in this manner: command to the patient that he put his head in your hand, then suspend those vessels on the whole line according to his wisdom, and let the lines be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two lines by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil as forces those vessels subtly, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see remove those vessels out of the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of spatulas, and make this work at the hour of midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut further than those vessels; and when you will have done this, then distill in the eye collyrium green and red for to corrupt what is remained of the blood vessel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot gather all of these in that hour, make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and the abscess is sure to be hot, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and with sharp medicine according to those that I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut on the abscess, where it should die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then the king has all the instruments of this form; and it is called “sharp chief,” and it is made of iron one chief point, and it is pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that this corruption is removed; and do this several times, then return the place to medicines drying.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is sewn and flesh grows, and the body of the bow is sewn together, and it remains so for forty days, and it does not renew and is not bad pus, know that it is healed; if this is not the case, then there is no other remedy but to bring the fistula back to its original opening according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take one forest according to this form, and let the iron head be three angles, and the shaft be attenuated up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then put it on the bone below the tear duct, and move your hand from the eye i.e., 1 pock, then turn to the whole forest until it pierces the bone and he feels it through that which comes in this if he holds his hand on his nose; and then return the place of dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the places, then go the matter to the nose; so is lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open fully and there is no disturbance in the nose or diminution, then you must bind the patient; then cleanse, then place suction cups or a leech without harming to suck, then place on the eye i. one linen made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and apply a plaster on it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each one in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; then strain them from above with a hard bandage, and restart the suction cups to suck without harming; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the linen softens, then you must strain it a lot; then remove the linen after the day and the night, and if you see the eye repairing, it is good; if not; then restart the plaster and cloths and the linen and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the dislocation of wool
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, then open it, and there come forth fibers like .i. grains of resin, and it is astonishing to see; therefore if you see it covered, the work is such that you put a needle into the root of the lower part until the one above, then put another needle where there is .i. double thread from the tear; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the grape around it, and restrain it well, then extract the needle and put on top the oil-like half in abundance of an egg; and let it stay until the threads fall with the grape, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healed; and at times the wound is restrained by the grape each side of a circle of cloth, as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show great appearance, then pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes from the oil, and correct the albuminous moisture and lower the eyes, and enter them immediately; then extract it as long as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the  bow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This illness which is called "alcunnati"  is nothing but the bow that is assembled in the eye, seeming like an arrow descending, and it is not a needle; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a .i. prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from .ij. parts, and move it as much as you see the bow coming up to your eyes; then be ens fichie, and do not descend and be disordered the light, and the patient sees things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is an arrow, and if the descent of the bow is not arranged as we have said. so make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and make on the corneal cloth .i. point by the continuation of the conjunctive with the cornea and the corona, as much as the bow issues; and when it is issued, so distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then be cured of other cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the needles of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have seen the appearances of needles in division, and what is necessary to perceive; so in work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the light for the sun, and tie the healthy eye and hold it tightly; then put the paper of the eye on your left hand if the eyes are left, or on your right hand if the eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument that is called «almagda», or in your left hand, if the eyes are right; then place the tip of the instrument near the cornea by the width of a thread in that white of the eye to the part of the less tear, then put the instrument called «almagda» skillfully, and return your hand as long as it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the path almagda be at the middle of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black; and this is the cornea of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal tissue, and then put the instrument up to where the needle is, then express it from below one way after another. If the needle now descends, if the patient sees in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After rest .i. little, and if the eye returns to the second way, put the force with the instrument, and when it is ensnared and it does not rise, extract almagda gently by turning your hand poc and poc; and then return in needle a pinch of silk gem, and leave from that the eye inside. Then put outside the eye plugged or bandage half dipped in rose oil and in abundance of egg white, and tie with the healthy eye.  We, and those who are of our time, put on top as a common broth with abundance of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, because there are some men who have their eyes too hard, it is necessary that you take the instrument called «alberit», of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce therefore the conjunctive only, and do not go too deep in it, but make .i. it subtle, then put almond, as we have said; and at the completion of the work, equip the patient with .i. a pillow coming forward, in which he sleeps on his back in .j. a dark place; and be deprived of all movements, and eat light meats, and do not move your head neither to the right nor to the left, and be bound according to his disposition up to the third day; then untie it in that same dark house, and try his sight, and let him see some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not good that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you align this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If the abscess comes, that you untie the eye before the seventh day, and the address of this which soothes the abscess; and when it is appeased, then untie the sight and put on his face .i. an orilliet to cover any day, and be in that same dark house. And then go out of the house little by little, and be converted in his affairs; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country they made almond pierced, to which one sucks the water, but nonetheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of the forms of almonds, because those who do not know them see them; and they are properly of grain.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of these of this same subtlety, and the hind in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh from the nails
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes nails grow joined together, diversely, because of which some seem like scorpions with many feet; and if there are such [nails] where the flesh is cracked of a bad color, and some have flesh of good color. In that one therefore of these nails which is sound, and not cracked, it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands against the sun; and open his nostrils, and put the ointment on those nails, and rub them outwards; then cut what you are able to hold with a subtle sharp spatula on one side, until you know that this nail is entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that one cannot cover, then open it all, i.e., with instruments subtle and light, so that nothing remains; and if without a sore or abscess, then support it as is fitting; and if it are malignant abscesses, then haste and cauterize it until the blood is seared and all the pus is removed, then put on either oil or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nose works and moisture comes as far as the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as fittingly, know that there is raw flesh in the bone above, so that the instruments cannot come to cut; therefore it behooves you to put there i.e., a thread of linen a bit thick, and be bound by hands ours, and have between each knot a space i.e., an inch or less; and put the patient's head with the thread in his nose at its tip, and pull out gently until it comes through the nose inside the mouth; and many times do the children in school so, and it is a light thing to him who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and feel each after the other carefully as those who are or thread. Do this until you know that the threads have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this i.iij days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put on the nose a patch of wool for some days until it is healthy, and if there is need of drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, by which one distills the oils and medicines in the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, as a basket, and lead it so; and if you see fit, make a closed basket, and let the instruments be full for cleansing the head; and have one handle at the top for holding it when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the bone
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times at the head of the bone a sickness arises which is called "telul", and grows and becomes great afterward, so much that it is a terrible sight to behold; and for this it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning, and pull out all the bone, then put upon its place the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays to cut it until it is great, beware if it is hard, of dark color, of poor sensation: do not touch it with iron for it is an infected abscess, because when one cuts it any time, there comes great evil to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touching, not of dark color, and you see that one can entirely cut it, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure its place with things drying and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the bone is cut and sutured
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these work cartilages, it profits little, for in few men. It is therefore necessary that when this happens to anyone, see if the wound is fresh in all its blood; and then adjust the two lips to a stitch, then cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are already severed on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all parts of their core until they heal, then assemble the two lips to a stitch, and restrain them, and powder upon powder of dragon blood, and incense ground; and put on the powders a piece of plaster of strong or other binding plaster, and let it stay until it falls off by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or by thread, as I have made you know.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In men's mouths happen within the lips abscess hard, seeming to grains of times, and lesser and greater; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and fends upon each one, and take with pincers and cut in each part; then apply there after the incision of vitriol ground, until the blood be stanched; and then the leave of this, and cure the place with dry things until it be healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times flesh arises upon the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and leave to run the blood or serum; then put on the place vitriol ground, or other restraining and drying powders; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, so cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the deaf
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the tooth is black and yellow and green, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is smelly; so it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his cheeks be in your saint, and pull out the teeth or scabs appear, until there remains nothing; and thus do of the blackness and greenness, and jaundice and other spots, until they are removed; and if one removes those that are at the first reason, it is good; if those no, then re-begin on the second day and the third, until you have pulled everything out; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to pull out, according to what the work shows, because the razor with which one pulls out the teeth outside have other forms than those that are pulled between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you take care to drain as much as you can, because one should not do otherwise; for it is a very high substance until one has no excuse to pull it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to be treated, it is necessary that you be certain about the tooth aching. Many times the pain of the patient deceives and thinks that it is a good tooth and pulls out the good tooth; and nevertheless the pain departs not by this, as long as the evil remains, because we have already seen this with our patients; and when you are well certain about the tooth aching, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth in all its parts with a spatula strong to guard the gums from all sides; then move it with your pliers or fine tweezers at the first pit and pit, as long as it is well loosened, then firmly secure the pliers; and let the head of the patient in your lap between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth straightly without breaking it, and if it does not jump out, take any of these instruments and put them inside each part lightly, and move it as you did first. And if the tooth is pierced and broken, it is necessary that you fill it with dressings, where the holes are; and if you extract it subtly with pliers, that it does not break when extracting it; and it is necessary to work very wisely around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And then be careful that you do not break it, and leave a part behind, and return to the patient by the malice of the root greater pains than the first. And beware that you do not do as the ignorant healers do, who by their haste and boldness sometimes break the jawbone, and do not bring about what we have recounted; but they often bring about great illness by the lesion of those roots that remain, or by the jawbone that they break, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or oil and salt; and if bleeding comes out, which often happens, apply the place with vitriol powder; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, which one must first use the teeth, are to be long points and large handles, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of good iron, and be toothed to hold well.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains in the tooth, it is necessary that you put on top of it cotton moistened in butter, one or two days, until the place is softened, then you put in the pliers which are called "algefri", because the head seems like a beak of care; and be inside made also like a file and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and there put the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a spatula, because this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be thick and strong so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with these, it is good; if these do not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which this is the form:
