et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments which are in front in the shape of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument should not be able to break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the illness show them, because there are such diseases where the old ones do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others; and if one does not break the bone or the other bones, or where it is possible, then seek the instruments that are necessary, as I have said, and help with gestures, this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but it can hold and remove; and then restore its place with medicines suitable to this, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, so the king has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and even in virgin women, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file or polish it; therefore, the chisel; and if it is next to the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and is similar to 1 small beak, and be of sharp iron at its tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cope little by little in hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, if the file of a certain form like this is.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file used to make needles; and in filing the tooth little by little in hands for days lightly, so that it does not move until it is finished; then the plane at the end with no scratch, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bites the tongue, then it is necessary to file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth in front moves forward, or by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press so that it moves unless it falls out, and you have cured them with medicines constricting, and this does not work; if it is necessary to restrict it with a gold wire, because the silver wire becomes green and rotten, but the gold never changes; and be the wire moderate nor too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see to tighten the teeth, so take the wire and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the diseased teeth, if there is one or more, as long as you come skillfully up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering up to the place where you began, and pull your hand subtly and skillfully, so that it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the ends of the wire with pliers, and assemble them, and put them between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can remain, and if it unties, or the wire breaks, then bind it with another wire; let it remain and serve thus all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the tightening of the two healthy teeth, and the two diseased ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, so it is put back in its place, fresh to fresh, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and suffering, and at some time the form of a tooth of bone of beechwood is made, and it is put in the place where the deficiency is, and it is restricted as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	At no time is this ligament that comes from below the tongue or nature, that one is born thus; or by accident of a suture wound; and the work is such that you operate on the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue. Then cut the nervous ligament wide, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place; and if there is hardness or something else, and this is from the closure of a wound, then put the awl and cut wide that ligament; and guard that the incision be not too deep, for the artery which is below. And when you have done so, raise the cloth of rose water and of asil, or of cold water; then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and tie the sick person's head each night, that the place may not close together. And if bleeding occurs, then put on the place vitriol ground; and if the blood does not stop, then cauterize it with the lentil cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of rusty color or black or hard, so that the sick person does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards whiteness, and there is moisture, then put down the awl, and cut it with a fine spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other. And if the blood does not stop at your work, then put on top ground vitriol until it is stained, then return to your work as long as you extract everything; then raise the cloth of rose water and of seil, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	At times, boils come from within the throat which are called “godath,” and they properly call them the two almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small size and with a dull color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and its root is large, do not touch it with iron, also to avoid the loss of blood; but leave it until it is dead, and afterwards you will cut it open, or it would burst by itself; and if it is of a whitish color, and the root is subtle, have your instrument ready to cover, but first look if the abscess is cold, resting and calmed. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his cheeks be on your side, and open the mouth and take the serjans between your hands, and press the tongue down under the entire instrument, from this comes the form; and let it be of silver or of iron as subtle as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue down onto this entire instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the needle and put it into the almond, and pull upwards as much as you can; and pull nothing else from the tissues with it, then cut with the instrument, from this comes the form that resembles a force; and nevertheless the chief are curved, and one place the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or of steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, then cut with tongs, from this comes the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be trenchant on one side, and on the other side no; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and cold and thus, and if there is a discharge of blood, gargle the patient with water, or peels of pomegranates that are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is cleansed; then cure it until it is healed; and no time arise in the throat other abscesses than the two almonds, so cut them as the two almonds, always.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I medicated a woman from an abscess that was born inside her throat, that is to say one abscess of small size; and I had very well closed the whole throat, so that the woman could not expire through the conduit which was obstructed, and could not eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained so one day or two. And the abscess was so raised that it had been put two fingers by the two openings of birth. I therefore immediately, and tied in one a needle, then pulled out the trail, and in a large portion of bowel; then refit another piece in the other opening of birth, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; after tying the needle in these abscesses, and cut a part, and there came out only a little blood; and thus was unstopped the conduit of the throat of the woman, and began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew back again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I engaged it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus remained without growing; and I left these parts, and know only that God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the grape is ripe and it is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is very large and round, it is called "grape". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the poultice of the abscess has been calmed, and it is thinner, then it is necessary for you to cut it; and the one that is round assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of a reddish color or black, then it is necessary for you to make the incision of it. For there is great peril on the patient. It is therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument which we have spoken of before; then insert the needle into the grape, and remove it as little, and cut it at one or two instruments which I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, it grieves to the voice, and to speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient has fear to be cut, then it is necessary for you to use him an ointment at the cauterization of the sense of fear. And the manner of the cautery is sharp.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put on his head a hair or where one puts the medicine, as the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument to all the medicine above the grape; and the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and the muscle run from his mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the windpipe; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it onto the grape, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it burning and the bite of the medicine is calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton into the channel above, until the cotton hardens on the grape; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five days. And if you need to recommence the cauterization of the medicine, commence it again, and after the cauterization, wipe around the grape, with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and be raised with cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, nor cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in one pot, and put it inside, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and within the pot have one instrument shaped according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And let it be of silver or iron, and let one of the heads be put in the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises to the uvula by the cane, so that the uvula is mortified; after this do often, until the uvula dries, and guard that you don't do this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, because many things happen; and don’t make this unless it is at the declination of the hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, then take a cane and put inside its head a piece of egg, so that the mouth of the sick person doesn't have too much heat; because the piece of egg does not let the vapor burden the mouth, and this is a good cure altogether safe.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is lodged in the throat a bone or spine of fish, or any thing; so it behooves you to draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see move the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, it behooves you to make the sick person vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if it will draw out the thing dry by vomiting; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one morsel of dry bread; and tie to the sponge one thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will lodge itself, and then you will draw it out further; and if it does not come out by what we have said, then take one instrument of plumwood according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have the head high raised; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all come to naught, nor thrust in the bone; and move it is better that the patient thrusts the instrument, for he will know whether or not the thing is harsh; so thrust down, or draw it forth with all the instrument equally, as long as it be forth.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the bleeding of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	At no time is the bleeding of the throat treated with medicine, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when those do not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sun, after you have pressed his tongue with the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the bleeding, so treat it with all .i. a small pin, or with delicate forceps that are good for this. And if that does not work, take a  sheathed chain, and put it into the throat of the patient, then thrust in one end of the chain .i. hot iron, and do this often. And if the patient remains feverish all day. Then take a full .i. cup of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with his hand often; and as soon as the bleeding feels the water, so it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have spoken of in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will surely fall. And the manner of the fumigation is that you take one pot where there are burning coals, and let the bottom be covered with a veil pierced in the middle, and in this pierce the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes up to the throat; and the throat will now tighten, and if it does not fall, then begin the fumigation again many times; and suffer the patient thirst, and give him salty and other foul things to eat, and let him drink no water; and then the necessity that it goes out by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the throat is, when it can be seen, like tongs curved so that they can enter into the throat; and it has the semblance of a bird's beak, and it has an asperity of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many resemblances of abscesses are, according to what the remembrance comes here after from one and another in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and in size; and it is in .ij. manners that one is in its same semblance, and from those which it holds moisture. And the second manner is for the places where they are on the body, because the abscesses of the head are other than those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are other than those which come in joints, and each one has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if abscesses one should not pierce, as long as the boil is mature according to its fulfillment; and if there are some that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their fulfillment, such as abscesses which are near joints. Because when abscess comes near joints, and one lets it be until it is rotten inside, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, for this reason it causes contraction in that limb. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; or if it is near the foundation, pierce it thus when it is mature; and it is not fitting that you pierce an abscess ripe without complete digestion fulfilled, except for the one which is near the foundation, lest it be perforated too deeply, and become elongated inside, and there comes a fistula; and be unable to heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is mature according to its fulfillment, and that is when the pain is appeased, and the part of the fever diminished, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the shaking and the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the piercing where the most dependent part of the abscess is, and where it appears to bulge; and be the piercing long in the body, and if the abscesses are on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their places equally where there is no crease.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In these that suppurate, according to the member. And when an abscess is in its fleshy place, it is as good as you let the perforation until it is confirmed in digestion accomplished, as we have said. Because if you pierce it before then, it will lengthen the body of the pus from it, and it is full of much dirt; and by chance harden the lips and the depths of it. And to any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member has need of. And it is necessary that you bring in small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many cleavages according to the semblance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to sever the core, and cover; when it is become as one drapel, and is dead, then it is necessary to do as is done to buboes: and if there are any that are cut in three angles, and if there are any that are covered like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of anger; and if there are any where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and semblance cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have no chief, as a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it plainly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, then do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain a part; then plug the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing straight away; do this many times, little by little, until all the pus is gone. Similarly if the patient is of weak strength, or woman with child, or small children, or old men decrepit. Because the spirit trembles sometimes with the exit of the pus, that by chance he might die the patient, and you are not responsible for it. So avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain incision, bring in tents of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many perforations, then it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so that it comes one against the other; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have covered it inside out, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shaving of linen rags without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then untie it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, then bring cold water and apply it, and moisten one drapel, and put it on the place where blood is flowing many times. And if the bleeding persists, then bring government and cure, and the powders that I have said in hand here in this book, and if it is in winter, and the place where the abscess is is very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on tents and drapelz moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the place is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on drapelz moistened in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and clean it, and cure it, as is fitting, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	Of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Of sores
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the incision on a pus-filled abscess and moist one, it is lighter because they are of little blood. And if in some of these abscesses or chiefs where there is no moisture, and of these I had seen .i. abscesses that was a chief of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and cannot break; and if one had made any incision on it, one would have done as well to him a wound like a stone. In other abscesses coming or chiefs, whether those that come at the chiefs of children and at the roots of ears, the opening must be always at the lowest point, so that the pus may issue easily; and the cure as it is fitting.
des scrophules	of scrofulous sores
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses happen at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come somewhere else or on the body, and are very bad, and are joined together with one another. And each scrofulous sore is properly within its own side, as the others and the abscess of the chief, as we have said; and the resemblances of these scrofulous sores are many. There are some that contain moisture, and some that are malignant who will not obey health. In the one therefore that you see of good disposition to touch, and is similar in color to the body, and mute on every side and is not at all close to the nerves of the neck or to the artery or to the vein, and is not very deep; then it behooves you to open it from above, and to make a cut of each part, and to put apart the two lips of the wound as in the abscesses of the chief, if you have need of it, as we have said. And treat little by little, and be sure that you do not open the nerve or the vein, and let the spatula be gentle and make no trenches, so that the hand does not slip, and look too far ahead, that you may not open what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not let you work, so put in the wound powdered vitriol, or any powders that restrain blood, and constrain the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. And when the bleeding is stopped, return to your work, as long as you accomplish it; then inquire with your index finger if there remain any small pustules, if you cut them and cleanse them. And if in the root of the pustule a vein is large, so it does not behoove you to cut that pustule at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and leave it hanging by it, without annoyance; then apply the wound of old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the whole pustule, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then when there is no more superfluity for the size of the pustule. It is necessary that you intend to cut the root of it, and draw pus, and sew it as we have said. Those pustules that hold superfluity, pierce where it opens more; and pierce it as before mentioned, in dependence, then administer tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, cure it with ointment causing flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of scabies
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of cutting open the throat; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squint, it is necessary that the slit in the throat called "epiglottis" be cut open; and do not help them because all veins and the pores of the sick are hot at these who have abscesses in the mouth, or in the throat or in 2. almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the pore, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below 3 or 4 circles with a small slit through the middle, between the two circles or by the quantity of the slit of the syfac, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those that are such are agreeable to the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long of length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat to the whole neck, then cut the keel until it comes to the channel; and shun the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the neck that flows out from the place which is broken, and by the lack of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which one doubts strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew them together alone against the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this juice until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect is in the lung.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, one cuts the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And for this, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And therefore they commanded to sew up the wound and care for it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady took one knife, and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called by her to heal her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and well that it had not yet cut a vein nor led further than the throat, and the veins were thereby brought out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I bandaged it, and thus I closed the wound, and I treated it until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and nothing more happened to the young woman except that she was hoarse of voice, and returned afterwards to her disposition;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for this reason I say that in cutting the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in the color of a wound, and it is much in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to two manners: natural and accidental; the natural has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners, of which one is similar to fat in us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it does not behoove to work to do fierce than in the one that is small, and prove and seek at all the intruder.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find him also like our fat, and cannot at any vein, if the cut, as we cut the ours, and the tail to all its hair, if there is any of it.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and encircle well soon, and the cure as it behoves, until it be perfectly healed.
des nous	of ours
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways there are to us, of which I will say all the appearances;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and therefore it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that a lesion is sometimes feverish and hot, as long as the boiling has passed, and the putrefaction is complete; therefore rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With us there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains one tumor, which is its own sac, and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a swelling, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to two kinds, or dry, or moist, and very colored as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the new wound, that you first examine and inquire into all the instrument which is called "entromissoire," according to what its form will be or chapter which comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses is that you prick or moisten the place you find in the abscess and turn your two points and points until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then that it be according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the entromissoire, and take care in those who jump for it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs short, whatever color it has, treat it as I have said of other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the cautery moisture comes back, know that it is fat, so treat it in a cross shape, and take it with tweezers, and gently scrape it on each side and cover the patch where it lies so you pull it out healthy with the needle.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot pull it out healthy, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it returns to us many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it remains for a while, and the wound pains him, apply to the wound some sharp corrosive powders, and restrain the wound, and put on top soothing things of an abscess hot, and care for it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with those things that cause flesh to grow.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is too weak or otherwise you are in haste and apply the place of crushed vitriol, and leave it for two or three days until the wound purges, and rests the boiling of blood; then return to covering those that remain from the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	See here the forms of the instruments for introduction, and they are of three manners: large and medium and small; and there are three squares that are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are of three manners: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses or fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like the needles with which one sews the sorceresses, and they are of citrine iron, or silver, and the yellow ones are worth more, and they are more tested in black pitch to encircle the borders of fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And they are of three manners: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the probes are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and so there are probes that have two borders of three manners also;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And so there are probes that have three borders, and they are also of three manners; and so there are probes that have two borders, and probes of a single border only, and they are of three manners; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these are those one makes cuts with, and there are some that do not cut more than from one side, which we scrape the nerves, for which reason one does not cut the vein nor the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these introducers are the spatulas put in handles so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one should not use them anywhere other than in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and under the armpits, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And sometimes one makes i.e. another instrument small, resembling the scrapes of fistulas, according to this form, for which one staunch blood
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And one puts it sometimes in the place which is healthy to cut veins, and arteries, and sometimes around according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like breasts of a woman;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, should be according to this form of these lines from b. up to g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape the fat, and apply the wound with medicine preventing flesh, then bring together the .ij. lips of the wound to suture, and care for it until it is healed
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	And if the breast is lined down and softened for its size as it happens to women, then make two cuts above on two ribs, by two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	So that one is held to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. until the line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and there administer what we have said of sutures and powders, and what is necessary in the care, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of blood flow, then you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it consumes the remaining and the grease, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the buttocks are kinds of hard scrofulous lumps or boils which contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those who contain moisture it is necessary that they be cut according to this form, from the line b. until the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care with ointment after this as long as it is healing.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to a boil, then treat it as we have said for cutting boils, and if the wound returns pus, then administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut, and the skin that is above is sewn together, then it often comes to abscesses, and just as well it happens at the vein swollen and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if the one who knows this is about the artery, then are the abscesses long from it being made.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when you feel it in your hand, that is to say, it's a tightening; and when this is about the vein, then there are signs of blood being pulled out.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it is folly to cover this abscess, and even when it is under the armpits and arms and neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to avoid the treatment of iron, and in that which is at the head it is also necessary to avoid, and in that which is swollen of artery making from above the long skin;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then operate the waist as one incisions, and departs beautifully the artery of the cloths, as long as it is uncovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then put underneath it a needle, and make it pierce until the other side, and extract the artery with a double thread in 2 lengths, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the 2 arteries which are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then point the place which is between the 2 links with an introducer as long as the blood which is there comes out, and be careful to the abscess;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the cure that engenders a bow, as long as the ligature holds;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure those who are anointed with this, as long as it is healthy;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	And if the abscess is about the size of the vein, then it behooves you to hold with your hand that which you can of the abscess to all the skin;
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	Then thrust the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and let there be .i. double thread, so that you draw it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	Then close the abscess, as I told you, or bind one of the two parts to two shoulder with thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you doubt that the thread is not firm, reinsert another needle through all the thread beneath the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess until the superfluities issue forth, then cut away the superfluity of the core and leave what is bound.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place on one cloth moistened in wine and oil, then administer cures of compresses and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses come in the nerves when they are injured, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And these happen more often in the shoulders and hips, and in all places where there are joints, and these are very painful abscesses, and their color resembles the color of the flesh, and is in more positions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is pressed, the patient feels pain, and it is not in the depth of the flesh, but under the heart.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and keep it still from all sides, and do not go forward or backward, or down or up, and the one who is in joints should not be covered by iron: for fear it would contract.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And he who is on the head or forehead, make the skin with the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, then suspend it with a cord and peel it, then remove the pus and stitch the wound together, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	At no time occurs in the bellies and nowhere else, and is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its likeness to fungus, and it has subtle roots and the head large; and there are small and very large ones;
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw one man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a fine root, and they were slightly split, and pus came out of them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6. And the work of the incision is that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul (likely referring to a boil or inflamed tissue) is white and moist and with a fine root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	If the cut is on a wide spatula, and are in your presence the cautery of fire. For in the cutting comes many times too great outpouring of blood, and if without you it is vain, then hurry therefore to cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	And if you see the patient is frightened and afraid of the incision of iron, then take one thread of fleece well made, and bind the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the thread of fleece until it heals the joint, and ceases by itself without labor; and if the roots are large, then have fear to cut even for the belly, but you may well cut half
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then cauterize it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and keep that you do not cover the pellicle which is of fox color and of poor sense and of milk regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an ulcerated abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil has festered
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterization of a wound or fissure of the  syphax, and it is on the belly and has some boils, as they have in other ruptures, or of blood that bursts from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from flatulence;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is by the rupture of the skin and by the exit of the pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from different exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its two sides it rises up, and then returns, and perhaps it is constricted, and grows much at the entrance of the bath and for hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, it does not constrain at all; and if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses are thick and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to windiness, so is the breath at touching, and the works are that you look if its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	So it is necessary that you leave the treatment. Because there is doubt and fear in it, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if its appearance is for the intestine or the belly, then it is necessary that you command the patient to keep his arm, and be stretched straight, then seize around the bulge.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to  move softly between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place you have marked with all the spatula.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then stretch the half of the abscess upwards to the entire big incision;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk tightly, and let it be joined to the linen bandage;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then operate on the half of the abscess extended onto the linen, and put your index finger in it, and search for the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught in the ligament, then untie it, and put the intestine to the outside of the belly;
