et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the boil, then take it at its edge, and cut away the excess;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery makes it contrary, or the vein, then go well around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads of silk, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross so that you make them pierce;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then restrain the abscess in four leagues above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave them there until it rots, and let the dead flesh fall by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is subtle and swollen, then treat it as is necessary, and cover the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as is necessary, and close the place.
dou chancre	for the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the appearances of ulcers, and how one must work on them with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and let us say that the ulcer is generated in the marsh, and great caution should be exercised in its treatment, and the ancients said that when an ulcer is in a place where it can be scraped like an ulcer that is in the armpit, and in the groin, and similar places, then one must remove it entirely when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not fitting that you approach it, for I have never healed any, nor has anyone healed any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the works, when it is in place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge at any time the patient of black bile; then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, then prepare the patient i.e. good place to make the work; then get your tweezers or chancre, and the hair on all sides, and the bone on all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow out completely, and compress the place with your hand or any thing, and if the bleeding goes against you of the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the bleeding is extinguished; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: so it is only; and one should not touch iron in these two resemblances: namely, tympanites and hydropericardium, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this resemblance of dropsy which is called “eclytes” with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, consider if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and solution of the belly and similar things; if one does not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must thus operate:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lift the patient straight up with your hands, and the ministers press the belly by pushing the water to the lowest part of the pelvis, then take the spinal spatula according to this form: And be sharp in .ij. parts at the point, and all ways do not be so much that it can come to the intestine when you put it in, and do not let it pierce;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then look if the dropsy is increased towards the intestines: then it is necessary that you cut into below the belly .iij. fingers straight above the nipple; and if the dropsy is by the disease of the liver, so be your incision to the left of the belly .iij. fingers; and if it is by the spleen, so be it to the right, and it is not necessary that the patient lies on the incision so that the superfluities do not run into the weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push it out, and lift your hand to the spatula entirely between the skin and the syfac as much as when scraping at the quantity of a nail or in which enters; then pierce the syfac until the spatula comes to the place eight, and this is the place of the water, then draw the water out, and push out this instrument from where it is, and it is like the form: And it is similar to a subtle silver chain, and it is made of arrain or archaut lighter, and in the part below .i. small opening; and on one side, .iij. openings; and .ij. on the other side, and .i. on the other; and the head is tapered like a feather, and this is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the head above is the ailment, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it descends now upon the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, for if you empty more than it befits in that hour, by chance the patient may die because of the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls faint, or he approaches death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the sick person signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now by the heart which stops the opening that is on the syfac, because of what I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin the instrument again the other day, if you see the patient suffering those, and treat of the water a small quantity;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this none day, and guard yourself from letting too much water drain until there remains but a little bit of water. And if you doubt about the patient, and you let him too much water, cure him with burial or hot sand, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun, and let him stay drinking; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	At no time are children born who do not have a hole in the penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place. If it happens so soon that it cannot perceive at all one spatula very fine according to this form: then put on the hole one clo subtle of lead, and tie it and hold it thus for three or four days and when he wants to make urine, let the closure be removed, and make urine, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose hole is small, if they are medicated with the lead clo as we have said, it will widen. Those who do not have the hole in its place are blue because none are born who have the hole at the head of the penis, for which reason they cannot urinate before they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot come to the urethra, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies often on his back, and are the head of the rod and the cup as well as the waist of a pen, so that the pierced one falls in the middle, as it should; and guard against bleeding that comes many times, and if it happens, with the sponge of those who sponge blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples on the rod
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blemishes come in the rod, and it is a foul appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so it behooves you to prick them with one subtle needle, and scrape and cleanse them all, then put upon cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with diaficon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess is bad, of bad color and afterwards, then it is necessary that you bring it cautery. When you have cauterized it, and if the abscess is in its entirety on the edge, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the abscess which is inside first; and when it is united, cure the one outside. Because when you cure it altogether, it is not at all assured the joint of the edge that it will not be pierced, and comes blackness and corruption in its edge and where the opening is; therefore it is necessary to shave away all that which is black and corrupted, then place on top the ointment of honey and flour which is made of apple tree bark and vetiver, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form: The cauteries help two situations together: that is to say, for bleeding and for corruption; and if the joint of the edge is corrupted and retracts, it is necessary that you put or conduct from the edge a chain of plank, and piss the patient among; and when the skin is raised at the head of the edge which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with one instrument shaved, until the ties are loosened, and the joint of the edge is delivered from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a grievous thing to devise these, then it is necessary that you scrape it with one spatula from the head of the edge and of the skin; then sever carefully between two, and place there one subtle drape of linen soaked in cold water, so that it does not raise.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a wound of continuous bleeding like other wounds; however, when we perform this work by our will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest to salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not say circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have nothing more than what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have wanted the most part of the masters and healers who performed circumcision around i.e., in one dal, and with force, and a whole new knife; so it was the worse for them because there are two cloths, and by chance if one cuts the top and leaves the bottom one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the wound should be covered, and the pain is doubled, and in the purification which is done by the dal' it isn't assured the point of the member; and in the purification of the knee, by chance the iron escapes, and the work runs, and many times they are born as if they don't have need of purification and I have wanted.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the purification which is done with force to all of the thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut well just as much above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, if it cuts equally in one thing all of the soul tenses; but that the thread is well is twisted around the skin; and be the manner of the first work so that you make the child think, if he understands, that you only force him to tie the thread around the rod just so much, and then let it be joyful in all ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then make it be between your hands straight, and place the forces between your hands or below your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the handle and blow or heart, and pull it up until the head of the handle is in; then cleanse it well of the filth that is assembled there, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it below .i. pock at .i. other lien; and hold it as .ij. days by the second lienure to the pouch and to the index finger, and cut between the .ij. liens, then lift the heart above gently and pull the head of the handle;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let it correct the blood pock and pock, because it is the muedres; and put powder on and on the powder .i. drapeil glued with a yolk of an egg cooked destempreit'd rose water, confited with rose oil well and fresh, and let it remain until the next day, and cure of another cure as long as it is sanez.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the cleansing is this: the two heads should be held and should be sharp, and the heads are also as large as the hand equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the purification is when the kerchief inside is at the incision; therefore it behooves you to extend it to your finger so that the leaf makes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then take tenaculum and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they are three days and what is below the shaft is swollen, then let it be until the abscess has calmed, and lightly exfoliate it; then cut it as much as you can, and guard yourself from the part of the shaft, it will not harm him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the wound of things suddenly with powder, which we have said or treated of powders, and if you cut the kerchief excessively, and it goes upward, it will not harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to an obstruction of the stone, or blood congealed, or bowel, or flesh tumor, or similar things that we have said in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone in the urethra or neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent on his knees; and have their feet placed on their back, and extend their belly from the upper part towards the back, and restrain the patient's legs as much as possible; and therefore the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone upwards, so that the urine is released;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument that is called "syringe," of which this is the form: and it should be finely crafted silver, light as a bird's feather; and the handle should be one palm long and a half, and should be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take one double thread, and tie to the head one pock of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin of an egg, and make the patient sit on one seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and water tempered;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then gently put the syringe in the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis above towards the bottom; then put the syringe forward up to the bladder, and the patient feels it coming up to the void thing, and this is not done according to this order unless for those who guide or where it goes is twisted; then be the thread all the wool pock and pock, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it further, and do correct the urine;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and restart the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	of the bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood come in the bladder, or there is assembled rot, and you see it distill with sharp and medicines, so do to all the instrument which is called "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and has .iij. openings: .ij. on one side, and .i. on the other, as you see; and the tubes should be such that the medicine stops well the penis without addition, so that if one can draw out the moisture, and expel it when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you want to administer your medicines into the bladder, put the chief tube of the catheter in the moisture, and pull on the inner string; so that you will draw out the moisture into the catheter, and then push firmly the inner string back in; so that the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is the form of the subtle clyster with which one clysters the bladder: it is here:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is of silver or of brass, and the head is higher up; and below at one side or where the shoulder joint falls; then take a sheep bladder and put in it the moisture with which you wish to clysterize the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts forming a double strong thread, and heat one pot of that moisture on the fire; then insert the head of the clyster into the urethra, then strain your hand on the bladder throughout the entire movement of the moisture, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make one circle, and pierce it roundly around; then put one strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dial, and put inside that which you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction along with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as rains, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work with a cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder often happens to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder seeming like water in its subtlety; and it appears hare-like, and causes the patient pain in his penis, and he thrusts many times, and then finishes; and after much of these jumps the foundations are formed; and it is light the healing of children until they have 4 years, and it is very grievous in old men, and is as medium to those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the phlegm which is in the intestines. For it often hinders the searching for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, and push them out and move them down, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes rises from its high place; then have him sit between your hands carefully, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declining downwards; then the groin and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut above the stone. And if it does not fall to the touch of all, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is a grown man; and put it into its foundation, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, push it toward the neck of the bladder; then press upon your finger, and push it out to where you see to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him that he extend his right hand the testicles upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin which is below the testicles in the part where one makes the cut; then put the spatula cutting, of this it is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make between those who are between the buttocks and the foundation, not in the middle but on the side of the left hip; and be straight above the stone, and your two sides be either the foundation, and be the waist through the traverse so that it is wide outside, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, nor too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By adventure the press so the two sides that are either foundation, that it leaps outside without work; and know that there is such stone which has angles, and margins: if it is grieved to issue; and if there is one that is below, seeming like a glint, and rounded, whose exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To that one therefore where it has angles and margin, make the waist larger; and if it does not leap, it is necessary that you extract on the tongs which are as a file at the head, so that to move extract the stone so that it doesn't escape; or you put below the .i. subtle instrument curved at the head; and if you cannot engineer it thus, enlarge .i. pock the pierced, and if it is without decor, then strain the vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	and if there is more than one stone, put the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull out the tract, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more. And if it is very large, it must be sliced, and make a larger wound. For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes back through where the wound cannot heal; but nevertheless force yourself to drain it, or to break it with tweezers, as long as you pull it out in pieces
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have completed your work, apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and bind it, and put a damp cloth over it in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then support the patient on his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, wash the place well with oil and water, then treat it with diaphania ointment and basil oil, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the bladder, and because of that urine is retained, which is known in such a way that without leaping with the urine: therefore you should pour it into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and burn it;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	then raise the wound of  acute and easy and from silk, and help him in all ways that you know, until he is healed; and it behooves that all the hours that you cure him, that you tie his two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is where it is conducted from the shaft, and tied within, and urine cannot issue; so cure of this that I say also, that you cut it many times, it is excused from cutting through this cure. I have already proven this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron in this form and be it at three angles, fastened into one piece:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then put the piece of iron into the shaft gently, until it comes to the stone; and turn the piece of iron in your hand at the stone, point by point, as long as you can feel the stone on the other side; thus soon will the urine come, then press your hand upon what remains of the stone that is inside the shaft. Thus soon it is broken, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread below the stone and another above, then make the shaft straight to the stone between the two threads, then extract it outward, and untie the threads, and cleanse the coagulated blood which is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stone is engendered in women, and if it happens at any time, it is the cure grievous, and is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is one cannot find a woman well knowing who undresses herself to the mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is so much deeper than the stone of the man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and great fear there is.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessity demands it, then it is necessary that you take a midwife well knowing, and at pains find one, and if you do not find one, point so much as one chaste mirror subtil; and present her a bail well knowing in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command her of the incision of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And look very well if the woman is a virgin: then she must push her buttock or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she must constrain it below her buttock, and she recommends that she push her buttock or on the sick person, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the buttock, where it appears swollen and feels the stone in that part; and do not move her buttock above the stone or below, and be the first incision small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then push the root into the buttock, if you feel the stone so close to the wound until the stone can possibly be brought out, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have veins. If you know these similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the stone doesn't come out, put ground vitriol in its place, and hold it for an hour until the stone is softened; then return to your work, as long as the stone is loose, and have the instruments that I told you about for extracting stones from men to help you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone doesn't come out, and it is an artery that is cut, put the powder on the place and bind it with bandages, and do not re-begin this work, and leave the stone and do not touch it, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided, and the parts are healed, then return to your work, as long as the stone is loose.
de hernie carnouse	Of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is under the heart of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and at times it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is i.e. another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have said; and these do not have this point no.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is so weak that it comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And at times it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colours: or it is declining to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this assembly, because if it is or white as we have said, so is the abscess re-joined, that is to say long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the sides, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in the proper cloth, then is the abscess re-joined with a part of the egg, and for that reason one thinks that it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the sides and the white as such, then one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, you must probe the whole introducer quarrell, for its form is before this.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this therefore which comes after the introducer, judge of this which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then lay him on his back, on a thing slightly high, and put underneath him many blankets;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart from the sides;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spoon-shaped instrument, and cut the skin of the sides among them from their length up to near the armpit, and let your incision be completely straight when dividing the skin of the sides up to the white bone, and peel it carefully according to your strength;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the  syphons plain with water to one inch wide opening, and draw out all the water, and then put your bandages, and hold the syphon upwards; and do not touch the heart of the coions, but only the syphon; cut all or in pieces equally the rib of him subtly, that if you do not cut it well wisely, it will return the water.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the leaf has fallen during your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the syphon; then assemble the two leaves of the heart of the coions with one suture, and then cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the leaf corrupted by another illness, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspensory, fearing the outflow of blood; then cut the coion at all the suspensory, and draw out the leaf, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the point is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; so cut the other part just as you did the first evenly, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound linen moistened with rose oil;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put outside another linen moistened with wine and oil, and put on top the two pads, and put above cloth doubled, and tie it up over all the linen that is according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and put them in the shape of this lamb's wool according to this resemblance and be assembled by stitching at the groin of the breeches, and one of the arms presses on the foundation up to the back, and the other to the part of the armpit; and the other two from the head on top of the two arms, and let the whole restraint be assembled in the buckle of the breeches;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes this branch of cautery is medicated in place of an iron knife, and it is that you take i. a subtle cautery knife, and cut the skin of the testicles, and be heated as we have said, so that the white syfac which contains the water is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac at once, and scrape it with this subtle hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And the cut in all ways that you can, as long as you scrape everything; and guard that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more saved; and moves guarding against hemorrhage, and measures than the works of a knife;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if no other thing makes you contrary, or abscess or running of blood or other thing, so cure that which makes you contrary, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, so administer perforation as I told you, and it is that when you are well certain by the significations that we have said that watery root is there,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	so make the patient sit on .i.  high seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below to all the spatula wide, and put the perforation long through the body; and let the openings be wide so that all the water flows out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the place and bind it, and let the rest of the water flow out, then cure it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white cloth does not let the water exit from the mouth of the wound, it is necessary that you pour into it a pen or the instrument with which one treats the water of the hydrophics, of which form is above; and enlarge .i. poc the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after .vj. months or until then, and when it is assembled as before, and so will pass the days of the patient.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the buttocks
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this root there is fear in more dispositions, for which it seems to me that one better leaves it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I will tell you the work and resemblances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and also to the genitals; and it is by many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	That is to say by excess of sour and acrid humors, which are spread to the genitals, or by percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and does not find any pain, and is a serious abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by chance some abscesses are fearful and piercing and of a bad colour, and sometimes comes from the inside of an artery or from an inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from an artery, then it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it is not proper that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	The one which is made from an inflammation of a vein is known by its disposition at the expression with the touch of the fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and one can well do the sizing on this likeness, and on the other parts;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the heart of the testicles, then being the ewe on high, and the shaft further from the white skin, and deliver the suspensory from all parts of the ewe.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the ewe is already joined with these new parts, then it behooves you to pull out the ewe, and cut it;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is in the skin, or in those things that are within the vessels, then it behooves you to deliver all of that membrane, and cut it around completely.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the cartilage is or its back, it behooves you to cut it all and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are accomplished, then apply the wound of wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the genitals
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling that of a boar's skin, with the softening of the genitals
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient moves grievously when he goes
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the cure of this disease is as well prescribed as frighteningly as this one before.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on one raised seat, then put the suspensory of the groin low to their two thighs,
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	To all the vessels that are near the penis, and the masters braid them, and they stretch them out.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	Then cut with a sharp trowel wide through the vessels, until they are uncovered.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	And then peel from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then put a needle where there is one thread doubled, and tie it to the first place where the vein came from, and tie it straight to the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then cut the flesh in the middle straight, according to the length of the body, and treat the corrupted humors.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then cure the wound as with the others where one avoids a bulge, so that no vessel flows that nourish one of the sides;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for by those nothing comes from evil, and if all the vessels come alive, then it is necessary to draw the sides towards all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the flesh does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dries out and cannot be aided.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the shoulder
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The happenings of this damage are by the section that comes or shoulder, or the extension on the belly in the part of the angles, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rupture is either in the shoulder or of the extension of it, and come these 2 manners of much from causes: either by percussion, or jump, or by thrust, or by lifting heavy loads, and by similar things
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when this is of the extension of the shoulder, are that there is poke and poke, in long lengths, and does not come suddenly
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And the abscess is even up to the shaft because the syphac tightens around the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the syphac that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears diverse, under the skin close, and this for the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the syphac.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are caught with it, and are held in, and cause great pain to suffer for the patient, even when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, therefore it behooves one to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to draw the intestine into his hand within the wound, if it can enter.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then either hold it on his neck between your hands, and raise his hips.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch the heart upward, and cut all the skin of the scrotum long;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then put within the folds of the loin two needles according to what you need to open the wound, and so that it can pass through;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then peel away the skin that is beneath the skin of the groin, until the white fat is uncovered on all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then put your index finger into that which follows the groin, in that which is between the white fat that is beneath the skin of the testicle, and between the second fat.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	And depart that which is behind the testicle, and between the second fat; and then move with your right hand into the core of the groin, and having the white fat on top to your left hand, and lift the testicle toward the waist.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And command the minister that he extends the testicle upward, and unties that which is behind the ligament.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and if there is a point of the intestine wrapped or white as hard, and if you find no such thing, put it into the belly below.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	then take a needle or one thick thread made of ten threads, and put it into the back part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the buttocks; after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear from the threads until there are four threads;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then assemble them one above the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the syfac, which we have said is below the skin of the buttocks, with a strong ligature of two parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the threads around the hairs, and tie them formed of two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter in, except for an abscess which may come there;
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and place the rope straight according to the first rope long two of that one, and after those two ropes leave the remaining length which is under the curve of the shoulders the width of one finger.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after that all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the shoulders as long as it does not touch the bone, and the bone, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then administer wool moistened in oil, and place it on the wounds, and put back the rope that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never once is the white part of the face (the shoulder) that we have said cauterized after the incision, out of fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens many times, and leave the wound as long as it bleeds through it; and if it delays in healing, then be it raised with hot water, and put upon it what we have said, until it heals.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound with other cures, as long as it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I never saw anyone who dared to do the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like the root which is attached to the vis, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the cut above or lightly below;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut it in half, and cure the abscess of those who work, as long as the vessels flow; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes a rupture comes in the bowels, as we have said, and open them; and do not let any of the intestines fall out at the anus, and if any do fall out, it is bad, and repair it immediately;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and nevertheless if it remains too long in this position, the wound or fistula grows larger, as long as the intestine protrudes;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens by the extension of the sinew which is at the angles, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and swollen its places and open;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and it is that the patient lies prone on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture inflated with a width according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the sinew which is below the skin that follows it, then take the iron and place it on the open place of the sinew;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and he presses on the front of the belly, then sews the two appearing eyes of the fig on the top of the thigh, and sews one and the other.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then he removes the top of the thigh, and does not cut of the fig nor extend anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the root of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then he cures it by the cure of wounds. And when you cut the threads, if he cleanses and cures the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The fig is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved to this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times is softened the skin of the testicles in certain men, because those which are inside are softened, and it is made to be seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and one cuts the skin which is softened on the natural skin; then assemble the two lips with a suture, and if you see, first suture the superfluity of the softened skin with three or four sutures firmly; then cut between the sutures, and cure as the other wounds, until it is healed, and throw away the thread.
dou chastrement	of the tightening
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that tightening is common in our law, and for this reason I would like that I do not speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two manners: one of which is that the wise men know how to answer when they are asked, and know the cure; and the other because we often need tightening of some beasts to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts. I say therefore that tightening is done according to two manners: either by attraction or by cutting. In the one that we do by attraction, we make our sit the beast in hot water until the testicles are softened and pliable; then taking them in your hand, as long as they are put back and you no longer feel them.  Of the tightening of size: it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut on each testicle one cut, when you have well scratched them; and leave no prick of the syfac and the subtle syfac which is on the vessels; and this manner of tightening is more mature than the one that is done by attraction, because at the attraction by chance nothing remains of the testicles, by which the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.
