Hermaphrodite is according to two manners as men: the one if between the two sexes it appears also as the figure of nature of a woman, where he has hair, and sometimes in short the urine.  And the other manner is in women, and has on the pubis also like a penis and two sexes. And the cure of the man and of the woman is that you cut the charted parts altogether, and cure them as other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine leaps through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tenting is a charted growth on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure. It behooves you to shave the superfluity of the tenting with your hand or tweezers, and cut it lightly; and don't go too deep, lest bleeding comes from it, then cure it with another cure until it is healed; and there is another char that arises at the mouth of the vulva, and the clittoris, and by chance leaps out, and according to its semblance like a cow, and for this reason they called it in ancient times "cow disease". If you must cut it, as we have said about the tenting, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	of erratic if is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accident by disease that comes to it; or it is by flesh joined, or by subtle syfac or thick, and it is made in the ribs, or in the side, or below, or wherever; and prevents conception, and childbirth, and by adventure the flowers to have; and the knowledge of these is by the regard of the bailiff. If the stoppage is near appearing, if it wants at its two parts or at the back. If it is subtle syfac, and it is near two levers, then hasten, and do this: put your two fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then having formed the two levers, as long as the subtle syfac is gone, and the stoppage is over; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the place, and lay the woman to bed every day, so that she cannot move. And if the syfac is hard and thick, it is necessary that you cut it with a spatula resembling myrtle leaves. If the stoppage is of flesh born, then suspend it at the knee and cut it; and have the medicines astringent blood, as acaice, dragon's blood, incense, together with an abundance of egg; then administer a bandage of wide cloth, so that the wound cannot close; and thus for a long time, and administer a tent of dry linen; then cure it with other cures until it is healed. And when in the ribs comes flesh born, then it must be cut according to this manner, unless it is inflamed abscesses. For the inflamed abscess that is in the ribs, one should not touch to make.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without accustomed short and when hemorrhoids are old they become thickened; and we have said in the division the similarities of them, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve healing. I say that hemorrhoids and the thickening, when they are deep in the flesh, and they do not appear to smell, unless it is cured by iron. Those that are at the mouth of the flesh, one can feel them, are those that one can cure. It therefore behooves you to put the woman in a cold house, then are the thickened ones with tweezers, and the cut in their roots, then powder above medicines restraining blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet out into the open air for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there comes a discharge of blood, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranates and galangal and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and aisil, and make .i. plaster on her back. And if it hardens, it is good. If this does not happen, then you make air suction on the back and breasts without injuring them; then take linen, and soak it in plantain juice or in elderberry juice with old wine, and make air suction on its place. And when the abscess settles, cure its place with ointment until it is healed; and the one that is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to .i. sharp chief, so it must be cut as I have said about the thickening; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the flesh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come in the flesh, such as chancres and purulent abscesses and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have said in the division. It therefore behooves me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the flesh, which is not of the abscesses that boil well; and if you want to know the work of iron, look at whether the abscess is aggravated at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red you can see it.  Therefore do not hasten to pierce it, but let it die down until the pain is appeased; and then make the patient sit on a small seat, with two small seats where he leans, and supports his back and brings his feet together from the legs; and let his hips be spread apart, and put his arms below his knees, and tie them well with a good linen; then draw the person towards the right side of the body, and administer the instrument which is used to open the mouth of the flesh, for this comes after. And it behooves you that when you want to administer this instrument, that you put the tip first in to know the depth of the flesh, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it behoovees to cover the depth of the flesh with cloth, so that the instrument does not hurt them; and it behooves you that he put the tip of the instrument above, and hold the instrument. And when the abscess opens, and one holds it gently by hand, it must be covered at the head, on the spatula; and when the boil is emptied, it behoovees to put in the wound bandages moistened with rose oil, or green ointment; and put the bandage from the wound to the bottom of the flesh, and put over the flesh and above the palm of the hand a clean linen cloth soaked in water or mallows being boiled; then cure it after two days of ointment until it is healed; and some time lift the flesh and the wound with a clyster of water and honey, and then water or roots of lilies and long arisotle, being boiled; then return to the ointment. And if the wound has returned in the flesh, it behoovees that you guard against burning iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is first necessary to the midwife that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down, and desire to smell the air; then hasten the birth out of force, it being born; so know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and is the head first, and the second with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly so that the child comes forth quickly; for when it descends upon its head, then follows the second with it, and is cleansed the body of its superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For it sometimes comes upon its feet, and comes out toward the body or the shoulder, or the hands, or it comes upon its belly, or loin, and it is converted by chance on its neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary to the midwife that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes upon its head by natural birth, and the woman is in labor and giving birth hard, and the virtues of it are weak, then have her sit on a saddle, or let the women hold her; and rise its nature of oil or fennel seed that is cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs with the little spatula which here is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and cleave the secondine, and cut at its fingernail until the moisture that is inside is out; and grasp the belly of the woman so long as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it behooves to clysterize the woman with musk of fenugrec with oil of sesame; then make her inhale and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will be extracted. And if the two hands come out, then it behooves that you reset them gently poco a poco; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on one stool, and raise her feet up; then tip over the stool to the ground, and hold onto the woman so that she does not fall during the tipping; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands at the knife which is beforehand placed, and extract the child, and reset it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the issue of the child on his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes on his feet, then it behooves to push upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then he turns it back and forth, until it is even.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then seize i. the feet and extend it back and forth.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Unless it jumps up to the hips, if commanded to grasp, and make it sneeze from condition.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come as we have said, then take a handful of alum, and oil of sesame, and pounded gum, and grind everything in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then make him sit upright, seated down to below the ribs.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when it is softened underneath, make him a collar of myrrh, and put it underneath, and let him leave for an hour.
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make him sit on a seat, then make him sneeze and restrain his mouth and nose, and take his belly lightly, because the child is now jumping.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the exit of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, he puts his hands there little by little.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	Then either support him on his neck and let his feet hang down, and let him lie on a bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bend his hands little by little, and then take his hands on his belly, and take away the cushions underneath, until they are positioned down low.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	And if the child does not jump, then take his feet and move them forcefully, then move his belly upwards, and then put your hands in.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and let the child suck and suck; and instruct the woman to breastfeed him as long as the infant lives.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the issue of the child who comes out with a wide hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to devise how to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman rise and leave;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If it cannot walk, make her lie on a bed, i.e., a litter, and tie her legs together.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	Then administer the poultice that I have recounted;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	And if she does not give birth, make her sit on a seat, then study how to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	And draw out the child according to the natural figure, and make her sneeze, and command her to strain herself as long as the child is being born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the delivery of the child on his neck, and have his hands spread out, and his face turned toward the back of his mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is convenient that the midwife hold his hand, then turn it little by little, and the ewe lightly.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is equalized, put it on the soft flesh of the area and oil, as we have said, then command her that she move little by little.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, make her sit on one seat, and command her that she sneeze; and make the face sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner to all the spine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to treating in this manner to the entire spine, cut the spine with your finger, until the moisture is gone.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	And if the child can't breathe through their face and neck, cut the bone so that it is not held back, and kill the child;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	Then put the child inside, until you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman that she does not get pregnant again;
adonques si istra legierement.	therefore if it is gently pulled
de l’issue des gemelz	from the separation of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and do not live, if they may be named;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know these, that they are multiplied, and are severed by the sifac which divides them, which is tied to the bud.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And sometimes they come out as naturally as one under all, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come out roughly, then the cure as we have said, and let the bandage be subtle, and make it quickly and lightly what it does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do so as it is worth for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	At no time are formed in the marshes i. or ii. or iii. or iv. or v. or vi. or vii., or more up to xv., and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of his glorious sage,
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary that the bailiff knows all these things, because by chance similar things happen.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	if it is done according to what is right.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat the woman of the dead child or womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or she has fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, and her head inclined downward, and her legs raised;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister binds the swaddling cloth in two parts, where it is tied to the bed so that it is not treated in the descent of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the mare with moist oils with moss of holly and fennel and flaxseed, then grease his hands with these oils and these mulsilages;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then insert them gently into the mare, then desire one lung where she puts the onions that are suitable to these;
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take ward if the child is appeared that he descends upon his head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if he places the pins in his eyes or in his neck or in his mouth or in his palate or under the beard or in the armpit or near the ribs
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is on the feet, he places or pierces him and the sides of the feet.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he hold the pin in his right hand, and place the curve between his two fingers of the left hand, and thrust it with all his hand lightly, and place the pin in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the form of the pin:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	Then place against the other bone, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then make them even by moving one side and the other, so that they go easily in, and let the bones be toothed to hold them, like this is the form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if a part remains, then oil some of its joints with oil and put them in that part, and draw the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if nothing remains of it, then put this bone or higher than its place, and do so until it goes all the way out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be returned by constriction,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then you must envelope it with a bandage, until it is whole.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	Then cover the joint of the hand or at the wrist, and in this way you must do with the other hand, for two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the joint of the child is swollen and it protrudes, or there is an acute head gathered
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	If it is necessary that you put the pointed spatula between your two [parts], and make the point and draw out the water.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you shall do it with the instrument called "almidach," so that its form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and in the same way, do it if the child has a large head naturally.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	And then with pliers, draw out the bones,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the head is dislocated and it is forced back, it may be split, as long as the moisture that is or worse has come out.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot be brought out, cut it in pieces as much as you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you should pierce it until the moisture flows out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the application to the mouth of the well is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is stuck in the belly or in the breast, then it is necessary that you draw it out, that is, wrap a cloth around the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and make the belly or breast, until the moisture inside is dried.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	And if the other members are set in place, and the head remains
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	then have the barber push his hand into the joint of the bone, and pull it up to the opening of the joint;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then he puts 1 or 2, and the  treatment will be;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the abscess is retracted because of the hot cautery which has come there, it does not need to be worked on;
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	but one should administer moist and fatty things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and administer poultices, and  soaked in softening and moisturizing water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on his side, and you can put him straight, then administer what we have said in a living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if one cannot do this, then the limb should be treated in pieces, and nothing of the second part should be left behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, then administer what we have said in abscesses that come on the thigh.
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And if discharge of blood comes, then put it in vinegar for restraining, and administer other remedies to him.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one fetus had been killed, then conceived another on top of it, and refused death to the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, it came an abscess in the belly, and swelled so much that it opened, and began to great suppuration.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I pondered long, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and out came one bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was amazed a great deal because this one whose belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I touched the wound, and in my hands were bones, as long as the woman was getting better;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman lived a long time like this, and she had a little bit of flesh in that place;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have recorded this chapter only for those who, when masters find a strange thing, they may know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	how to bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the pressor, which we have in the books; and to two turns at two joints of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the shaft be i.e. two finger widths wide, and the margin of the trees i.e. must be, and long one palm and a half.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two limbs be two adjustments of this same shaft, which are fastened in one and the other, of half a palm long or one poke more.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two adjustments are put in the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, similar in appearance more subtle and lighter, be made of ebony or boxwood shaft, according to the appearance of pliers.
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and have two joints two fastenings, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see to open the mare [vulva] with all the instrument, so make the woman sit on one bed, the feet hanging and legs apart,
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then put the two fastenings together fastened in the mare [vulva], and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand with all the instrument, as you have done with tongs evenly, according to the quantity that you see to open the mouth of the mare [vulva], as long as the woman does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument are all surmounted, and are multiplied their likenesses; and when the eyes have seen them appear, so much is more hasty the work, and higher to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument that you have not appeared it, because their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is held at childbirth, it behooves that you command the woman to hold her breath, and then make her cough with condiment, and restrain her hands to her mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she jumps by this, well is it.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If this does not work, take one pot and make one hole or cover, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or any of them, be cooked or put in water on the fire; then put one end of a rope or opening into the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the marsh.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	And steam it until the vapor comes inside the marsh; then make it sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine is jumped upon suddenly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment and is not better, command the woman to wet her left hand in sesame oil or in the ointment of alum, and then put it in the area
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and look for the second one; and when she has found it, she grasps it and extends it little by little straightly, so that the hair does not fall out during extraction
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it must be moved gently to the right and left, and then pulled; if it comes and unroots itself
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the opening of the hair follicle is tight, we have said the cure of sneezing and fumigation with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not of all those that we have said, then guard that you do not use for the milk.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that he who is at the mouth of the mare, you tie him to the hip of the woman, then clysterize with ointment four-pharmakon.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if she carries and brings it back, and comes again for good; but nonetheless, when she carries if there comes bad smell to the stomach and head, and pales the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore it is necessary appropriate fumigations for those: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument for fumigating the woman at the time of childbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is like a dog in shape, and one puts the head fine into the nature, and the shoulders wide over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be over hot coals, and the tar as long as it is consumed, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation perceived, but it is stopped by subtle syringes:
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	so it becomes necessary for the midwife that she pierces that syringe at its proper place, and does not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and guard the incision so that she does not touch it;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on the half-linen in wine and oil, then the ointment's cure until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not re-stop, then put or pierce a cane of plomb, and leave him for many days, and be removed when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stupefaction comes from a closing of a wound or an abscess; so it is necessary to cover that closing; if it is cured, as we have said about the cautery of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are nodules, and larger than those that come near the outer foundation, or in the space of two parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodule is ancient, it works, and constantly moisture a white or subtle slime,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are pierced; and they are known by those who have them or excretion or ventorosity when the patient defecates, and perhaps in jumping some come out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if fistulas that pierce up to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and reach up to the junction of the groin, and up to the root of the thigh.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the fistula piercing at the base, and not piercing:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and is that you put your two index fingers or base, and insert a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has crookedness, then put in a tent of fine lead, or one hair of a horse, as long as you feel the tent or hair at your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come through by expulsion or windiness or liquid, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not pierce; so hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced to the bladder or to the passage of urine, so that urine flows out, and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced up to the hip joint, then the tendon comes up to the place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no twisting and the pain is within the joint, then it is that there is a bowing there, and there is no value in medicine or treatment by ointment.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these fistulas Persians have no cure except for labor, and vanity of the foolish miracles that intervene in them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In the one that is neither Persian nor ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you raise the legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined to his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put a tent of iron, or of lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tent comes to.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it near the base, then it behooves you to put your index finger there.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and then feel whether the tent has pierced it; and be discovered or you feel between your finger the soft flesh or the bone, then know that it is passed through;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if one does not work on it, one cannot heal it
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One says nevertheless that one can well heal none, but this happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid one does, if one carefully applies the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and it is all heated in the fistula, as far as it comes to the base; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these burnt charcoals are burned, which are resembling an owl's feather;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the cure of tents moistened in butter, as long as that flesh shall be, then the cure of ointment closing flesh and sewing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healed, it is well. If not, it cannot be healed otherwise;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent gets in and does not pierce to the bottom which is the foundation, and between your bottom and the tent there is a thick covering of flesh or fat, and you see the fistula at that which follows the covering of the heart;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward before the tent, and then the cautery after, as long as it comes to the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and shall be delivered the tent, and shall shrink; then seize those hairs which appear like a bird's feather, and leave none remaining.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood flows continuously, and goes between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery unites two good things: namely, the burning of these joined hairs, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the cure with tents moistened in butter or in ground herbs, as long as the wound lies open, and if the hairs are burned in the wound;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then cure the wound of inflammation by applying hard dried flesh, and are the medicines dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the bottom of the foundation, and is separated from the body, then put your finger or foundation in it, and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tent and between two is the cloth or the syfac or char, where it is close to piercing, then there is only a way of faith and hope by the administration of one of the three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can, put a tent and cure it like first.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not cut too deep, that you do not cut the holding that holds the base, and let the evacuations come by the way of the will;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said.
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps then it will heal, or you remove that covering and the membrane after it has been cut near its base, or by tent or other pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	Then bind the flesh flap that is in the wound, as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then study to restore the wound, and leave the fistula in the part outside the foundation; this is lighter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes fistulas are this way: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is or costs to the foundation near the skin above,
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if you take a tent pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And it puts one thread twisted in two, and puts the tent to all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pulled in the margin of the foundation within, then extract the thread from that which was pierced, as you put your two or foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and restrain one to the other, and let it be one day or two;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it no times, until the thread's ends that are between two, and stick together.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then cure the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it is not fitting to make a wound covering too deeply embedded, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the spatula spine from which one makes a fistula is quite useful, in one part and cutting;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand no, because one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners: or they are within the foundation, as much as a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short, they bleed.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	And there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and moreover there or a drop of citrine water or a drop of blood, and it has the color of the body.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	And the care of those who have them within the foundation, if it is that you command the patient to stretch for to go into chambers, as long as the foundations are wet, and the threads appear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you hasten, and can hold it with tongs, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	And if the tweezers cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with one drapery, or cotton, or a piece of felt;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and the strap them to your two hands, then cut them, and powder above with some hot powders that are in place of cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot be released, then have the patient do a clensing with a sharp and harsh enema to wash out what is in the foundation, so that it can be released openly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	and if the patient resists, and if the threads are strong from the foundation, then the cure is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you prick them with your finger or pliers, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner: take one twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread above and make the needle pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle,
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is double; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and extract the needle, and do this with all the others, and leave one for correcting the superfluity of blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation one draping moistened in rose oil or in cerate, and put it over the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until they heal, and when they are healed, treat them with ointments and other treatments, until they are sound.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of drying of the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of veins in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the sickness is old and the medicine is no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	Then it behooves you to scrape at the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the crust above, which does not allow it to become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then cure until it is healed as it should;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, begin the scraping again more strongly than before, until it heals well, and is scraped.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure until it is healed.
dou fremit	about trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	An ant is a small appearance made before the body, and it goes much in depth.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And no times finds it cold, and one feels it also like dead from trembling, and comes in all the body, and more to the hands than other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a  cane of an ostrich feather, or a vulture feather strong, and put that cane on the trembling, until the circles purple the trembling all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand to all the cane until you copy all around the trembling, and put it in depth, and pull out the trembling by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, so do this of a chain of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	nor pierce it, for to keep the two together, and move pressed And if you see it, so cauterize the furrow, as it is before or chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is a clyster made of silver or lead, or molten iron or mesh; and never are these instruments small and large, according to those who are administered them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore who are administered in the cure of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster is small and large if it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	And there is an opening or the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is pierced inside; and has on one side two openings, and on the other one;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	And it is the belly where one puts the medicines of a beast's bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small openings,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and between each opening one must place a space, then put into these openings one strong thread of twisted thread in ten or as much as it is necessary, and assemble the belly like it is a ram;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, if the one has the instrument in front of a strong thread, then clench; and this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then put it in gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the minister squeezes it with his two hands together until it is all full, then withdraws the clyster, and raises the patient's legs to the side.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to work well, so let the hair grow as much as it can; and if he sleeps one night completely, then it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cleanse him with a clyster for a disease of the stomach, and the medicine hastens to work well, so let him restart it until he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the base, or an abscess, so let the clyster be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle clyster on which the skin is restrained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; or we will say the cures of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by blows of stone, and cuts of sword and knife, or of spear or staff or arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or which are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with the wounds of the head simple, for remembrance comes in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is from a stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you greatly doubt an abscess hot: if the head itself bleeds from it and even if little blood comes from the wound, and the bleeding is on the contrary from the surrounding area;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	And avoid the patient’s repletion of wine and thick meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, let his meat be lessened, and drink no wine, nor eat much flesh;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, moistened cotton in rose oil only, or in wine stiptce;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess hot, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by the air, powder, that I will say a little after.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the art has moved it, then put on some ointment, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be joined together by tents, then join them with sutures, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed bone and cartilage, and only holds together by one point, then cover it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as roast and cooked barley, also poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find yourself with rotten skin and it doesn't reach the bone, so cut away all the rot and throw it out, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then cut the artery, and if you find it displaced, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and that you put into them this powder which unites as soon as the arsenic has worked.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is this: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood 2 parts; quicklime 3 parts, and grind the powder finely,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply it to the wound, and restrain it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bandage it well, and leave it unbandaged if it doesn't swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made with only quicklime, when one does not have the frankincense nor the dragon's blood, but that the heat has cauterized the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the wound has been moved by fire, even in the wound itself, then do not put this powder there.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	But put upon it certain dressings digested, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it heals.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then care for the wound with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine pincers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you hereafter the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, there is nothing else to do but leave it to heal and put nothing restraining on it, because it harms the nerves and causes them to retract;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put on the wound anything cold, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of them is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be warm, such as chaulmoogra washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cooked wash also in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of the mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so sew it and bind it with bandages, then tend to it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is raised and full of bump, then pierce it or lower.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut, and blood flows, then stop it, and clot it, and cauterize it as the matter requires.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the spine of the throat is cut, or the gullet, and the passage is guarded by which the meat goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	Then stitch the heart above the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then the strain occurs, and he leaves it for some days, then cures with ointment dressings until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then so desire.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, then treat them all with fire, and those that you cannot have, leave them as long as the wound is rotting.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and be careful to clear and align the opening.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then see if from the wound there is windiness as the patient gasps: know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	And if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, then do not put any powder to it in the first hour, nor bind it so that the blood does not remain in depth.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	And return to the heart, and apply it to the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but put attractive ointment on it, and bind it two times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there come not spasms, nor bad heart tremors nor pulling of the arm;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good arrangements, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal it therefore with tents and other dressings, as long as it is healing;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and work, know that there is an fistula; so treat as one must.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or deeper, or on the back, treat as that which is before.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it is large, sew it up; and if it is small, cover it with powder, and if it is deep into the bone, and has broken pieces, then pull the wound closed and remove the fragments if they are visible.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not visible, leave the wound to rot, so it will alleviate the extraction;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds to other members is judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the stomach's displacement
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The displacements of the stomach are great and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the large wound sometimes the intestine, or the nerves of the intestines,  are pushed in;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the suture is more troublesome, and sometimes worse the small wound than the great.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	Therefore one puts back into place intestines again, if one does not put them back hot in hot.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	Because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, so they enter less into place,
