et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	And because of that, the middle wound is worse, for that reason one resets the intestine to its place like the others two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And knows that rupture of the belly is according to four manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the suture of other wounds of the body and two other proper sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and nonetheless they are closer with the suture of the belly, and I will say one by one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine has come out.
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if something else is wounded, it is by one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said.
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Half a sponge or piece of cloth in lukewarm water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook in hot water with laurel and cypress and spice,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and boil the intestines until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes it is done with this restraining binding, and it moves only to loosen.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or ale and herbs be cooked.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by this it is aligned the entrance to little things.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make an opening in the wound with the instrument of which one uses to cut hemorrhoids.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is to move the spine
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut into it unless there is great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if cut inwards in the curve and not outwards, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the entrails are thrown out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if it is put back into its proper place according to natural form,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you have the power, because it is worthwhile.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the area below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower part of the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then place the head and chest higher than the lower parts.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	And also if a rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you set your attention on that part being higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	In small wounds put what you have seen;
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	Then you hold between your hands i.e., minister pitiful who holds all the tearing to his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and assembles the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common way of suturing,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and that you prick a needle or more, according to the quantity and largeness of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	Then leave from the head of the wound, that is, a space; and there put a needle where it has, that is, a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two ends of the skin with the two ends of the suture,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin within, as long as you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and assemble the two ends of the suture the four together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	Then the straining of a doubled thread around the needle of 2 parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	Then assemble the 2 heads of the wound together,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave 1 finger width of space, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	Then tie the thread like you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease to do this according to what you need of needles.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	as long as the whole wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and the needles are medium-sized, between fine and coarse,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the fine needles cut through all the flesh, and the too coarse ones cannot enter well;
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	For this reason they must be shorted.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	And it is not proper to put the needles too far out of the flesh and skin.
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not cut and open the wound before the soldering;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then trim the points of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or cloths at the shoulder of the needles to hold them in place
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them stay until the wound is closed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this way of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because one needle or two are used.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second suture is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you assemble the two ends of the skin and the two ends of the fascia together with a needle on which there is one strong medium thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you will have pierced all these four ends together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then withdraw the needle to the part where you have begun, in the manner one sews the garments;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each suture the thickness of a finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this suture is sewed on the man,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sew a wound that a knight had on his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was slashed with a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and was the wound more than a palm wide,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and was exposed intestines two palms wide,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and was the wound in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestine after it had been for twenty-four hours,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	And the wound was sewed up for fifteen days, and I treated it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the healers had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in one place where there was none to be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put a little clean cloth on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water and honey until it healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Or I will tell you the two proper manners of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and thrust it from the outside part to the inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When it has pierced the middle straight through, lay the point of the suture or thread where you have thrust the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side from the inside to the outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this sewing is that you sew as the furrier does furs
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the flap on one side, and take it back on the other, until the sewing is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of sewing, which Galens says properly
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is like how some make a  two parts together naturally
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the chiefs to the other chief, in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or chief of the miraculous proximity, and make him feel only that.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two chiefs of the syfac;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it felt from the outside part to the inside one.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as the two shoulders
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make one and the other feel from the outer part up to that within, in two other shoulders of the mirror which are on the other side
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the middle way of sewing and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	The Galicians say this word, and no one testifies to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must sew the belly with two needles, or there is thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew ropes;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitch more grievous than of the other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as the art has moved it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then set back the intestine and its covering; then put on the powder preventing flesh
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the art has moved it, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and stitch the thread, and weld the facets, and the mirror;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound as with others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you lack medicines, place upon it, as soon as it begins to gape open, old cotton,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need of other medicines in many cases when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not make communion to the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is fitting that you moisten the linen lightly with oil of temperate heat, or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the wounds, and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or rot in the joints, and many times it happens
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if the enemas of red wine help, and similarly if the rot comes as far as the intestine
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it pierces within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine that is called "young" cannot heal when it is rotten
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is because of the planting of the veins that they are, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the wire jumps from the wound, put it back as soon as it is fresh, just like the intestine.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has turned black, then you must tie the blackened part so that bleeding does not come from it.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries in it;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligament
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two heads hanging from the part below the wound all the way outward to align the extraction when the bones fall and the wound bends.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	If it can, restore it in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	For which I see that one man was pierced in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and from it he expelled excrement and wind;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I made his care according to what I could, and did not cease from treating until he was healed, and the bones joined.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him join, I doubted that the patient had poorly in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no ailment, but remained in better disposition, and ate and drank;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And they said to the experimenters that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he must be bound in this manner;
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take pliers with large jaws, then assemble the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	And when the pliers have opened the mouth, put it upon the two lips.
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it stretches its mouth open.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	And then cut the head off, and it stays so that it cannot be untied.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put one other bandage after it in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered
et cout la plaie.	and cover the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	That which chiefs gets hardened in the intestine, and brings no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can bind up the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestinal thread that is very cleaned
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this thread i.e., a fine linen thread twisted ,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it through the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of suture of limbs is not worse than according to the way of hope and expectation;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the vital intestines, there is nothing else or salves, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, it is universally called "fistula,"
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and also when it is pulled back and bent.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the truth a false knot hard and white, where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also pulled back like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in some clear jump back, and sometimes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is only due to one of the 8 causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, because of the smallness of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or for his wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because he has hard flesh inside and on the lips that does not allow flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or he has too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or his flesh is rotten and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is manner of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is tardy for digestion, and slow for health, and swollen by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones :
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the treatments of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Therefore it behooves me to make you know the treatment of fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	For there are fistulas that come from the large veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the sifaca, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it happens that comes to the property of the main limb, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of bad healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you are confident in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you see it clearly, if you take a tent of iron or tin, if the fistula is straight, then curved;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then enclose it with a subtle tent of lead;
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for lead molds itself to follow the twisting;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has openings by hand and you cannot well seek it by tents,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you clysterize by one of the openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for moisture goes from one opening to another, and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then probe carefully with your finger so that you know if there are bones or nerves, and whether it is closed in some way,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask carefully from the patient the pain that he feels when pressing of your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you will know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, if the cut according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and bone be the fault and the corrupt things that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the cure until it is healed
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well deep from right place, so it is necessary that you cut it as deep as you can
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put moist sponges in aguish medicine, and put them to the head of the fistula
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrupts the superfluity that is remaining at the bottom
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then he puts ointment healing flesh, as long as it is sound
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not sound by this, then cauterize it as we have said
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut into it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not strike or affect principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, so cleanse the king as long as the corruption is all removed.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with things that enclose flesh until it is sound;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not sound, and returns bowed as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not gone far enough;
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	If you uncover and want as long as you are at the bottom
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore its place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is thus healed, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this does not happen, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot reach it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there isn't another way to leave to nature
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can draw it out with pliers
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if you extract it with an instrument suitable for this
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, draw them all out, don't leave any one behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture acts against you, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if it copes with moisture and flesh, and delivers the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put something on the wound preventing rot,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the flesh around the bones rots,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and therefore they will have more easily the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	And if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you cleanse only as long as the blackness is completely removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of corruption, and comes up to the flesh of the bone.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary to be shaved and covered all the way to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to one man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was one young man about thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the matter came to the leg, and was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the surgeon, by their folly, opened it so much that the abscess burst open,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a great deal of matter came out, and it became a fistula, and there came much pus that all was wet and humid from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many a mirror they put to care for two years, and there is no wise man in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I was called upon, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and those who ran through the streets for a great distance.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and their bodies turned red from youth, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I put a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I then inserted and pushed into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came up to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was that one who showed me of the rotten bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption, except that which I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for long times, and could not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I removed it, and then I removed it, and I was concerned about sewing up the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not as much as I grasped around a palm of the bone, and the [he/it] was at all its flesh.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored him with medicines; and he was healed and joined quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it was no longer necessary to begin the work except for the weakness of the patient, who cannot endure
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For by the evacuation of blood often, but he was healed entirely.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in the place of the bone a hard cartilage was born, and he was of good disposition and had no annoyance or contrary in any way, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, then it should be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take one linen cloth and strain it to the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct anyone to stretch it upward
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another linen bandage larger than the first one, and tie it over the flesh which is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the bandage so that you pull the corrupt flesh downwards,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh in the place where you want to see, so that the bone does not whiten the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place one ember or a board under the bone so as to cover the corrupted flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to be as careful as one can see and feel the corruption, and to be even more careful other times.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open well, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover all the flesh; then place one ember under,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then so from one part to the other the corruption, and be the silk of the long of the corruption i.e. point, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and be the bone where it contains from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is nothing else to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is or at the heel of the hand, or or at the heel of the foot, then it is very strong that thing;
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nevertheless it is necessary that you inquire about that corrosion, how it opens to you.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or the nerve do not oppose you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the instruments and threads for covering these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of each,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and delicacy, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this it is necessary to equip each kind of operation with its instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and knows that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the manners of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so consider the instrument that you need according to this one that is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can be dislocated due to things inside, or outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated that corrosion with the cures of medicines, and they are not helpful at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cover that limb until the place where the corrosion comes from,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes through those of death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the fault of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards the blackness, then comes the corrosion of limb by limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes over the whole body; so hasten in covering,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as scorpions from the sea and vipers and similar.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corrosion is at the top of the thigh, cut it, and do not give him any space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, cut it at the joint so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes to the arm, cut it with the knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no use of remedies beyond the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And so do this when the corrosion comes or reaches a bone: if it comes in the first joint, then cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to a bone, cut the whole bone.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it ascends into the leg, cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means than to leave the patient to death.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	And the manner of cutting or sewing the member is that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister to the lower binding, and another minister to the upper binding,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you will cut the flesh that is between the two bindings to one spatula wide, as far as the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then cover it or skin it, and put on each side one linen cloth, so that the skin does not touch the healthy place.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if another wound and abscess comes to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the place thoroughly,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I shall tell you that it happened to one man in his foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had on it a blackness which seemed burnt by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion came first in the heel of his foot, until it consumed the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastily covered his foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long time after, it returned the corrosion to where two of the hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I placed on him things reverberative after the purification of the body, and could not cease the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he begged that I should cut off his hand, and I would not, for I had hope of reverberating the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and fear also if he cuts his hand, that it will not get worse,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the man's virtues were weak; and he despaired of all things, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he hastened to cover his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not recounted this tale for no reason, but because one does it differently if there is need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	At no time comes an abscess in its fleshy place, and stays so long that it causes great assembly of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then it bursts and perforates, and in jumping the pus, and remains its vessels, like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin that is above is as subtle as one fine sheet of fabric,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not pierce until the bone, nor until the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy",
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called «fistula»;
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so lengthened that it reaches the bone and perforates it, then it is called «fistula»;
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the treatment for this is that you cut all around that skin, and even when it is thin, like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not let it be healed for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you find that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not fully formed,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it thusly with a clyster:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look if the breasts are large, and the bowel within them smells foul,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then clysterize it with Egyptian medicine which is made thusly:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take oil, and lead, and litharge, equally, and put to cook in 1 vessel over the fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and make it in water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and in clysters put it in the stomach, and extract the pus;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine remain for two hours, then extract it pressing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the chest is purified, and fear is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and at no time is it cleansed with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is present, and it is that you take ashes from a vine trunk, and pour water on top,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it flow and cleanse, until you know that the breasts are well cleansed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then cleanse with a mixture of water and honey or where there is a bit of litharge ground.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you may cleanse with a clyster of honey and mellowed wine, for honey has the property of purifying and washing
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and wine makes the flesh red;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the breast is well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the clyster of those who makes flesh come out in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and that you apply a plaster definitive, and make it with rose oil and in wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you clysterize it with some medicines and ointments, of which I have said the properties or treated of the ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the chest is small, and the cannula of the clyster cannot enter it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then widen it with an iron a bit, and put inside a tent of the Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basil oil, as much as it needs to be widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, so the cloth and leave it only as much as the clyster can enter
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the perforated that hangs low is above, so the copes or lower than it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is in full, so do not let anything enter it;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	If it is arranged in such a manner that the belly goes to its lowest point
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the belly is full, so one does not allow food to be ingested
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast as well as you want,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	if it is arranged in such a manner: that the belly goes slightly downwards and nothing remains from the belly;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take medicinal ointments to put on the chest
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and place over it i.e., a cloth of linen that covers the whole chest;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then close with force the opening of the breast i.e., slightly wider than the first,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then place ointment above  i.e., another cloth according to the quantity of the opening,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it over the hole of the chest to align the rib, and remove not the large cloth outside except after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and the one that is out of the hole of the chest, often remove to remove the rib,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what came from the rib, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or indigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take ward if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has spread in such a manner and you see nature leaping above the chest wound
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breast is already healing, and approaches health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then untie it in the morning, or at midday, and when you untie the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if you change one other bandage, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the chest lies bowed ingestible after many days, know that the chest does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venoms cut after a long time, do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health approaches. Because there are men who take a long time to heal wounds and some do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the chest lies bowed ingestible after many days, know that the chest does not heal well;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast is slow to heal and is swollen, then apply medications drying in substance and dry in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as for example diaphani ointment, because it contains a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diaphan ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the essence of old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then boil it and use it; and the same thing made honey cooked mixed;
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when inflammation has ended,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then you smear it with one cloth, and place it on the chest, and at some time one administers a long rod;
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of the celestial lily, which is also like flour of vetiver and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simples or composites: grind them, and make it into powder, and put it on the honey that I have said, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption has advanced, and makes an impression in the bone, or hard parts, or limbs;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panares is an abscess that arises under the fingernail of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or by chance arises in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and one does not take care of it, then comes one abscess or another,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and corrode and cast the bow as long as they corrode to the root of the joint, and perhaps they corrode all of it.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corrosion to the bone, as long as there comes pain pungent, and is the shoulder two wide, and is the color fixed.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut to it with iron all the superfluity which is remaining from the joint,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses against the flesh, and it begins to prick, and the flesh
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you place a piece of leather under the nail that pricks the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and the top of it, and cut this carefully and lightly.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on top the remaining of the medicine hot and corrosive to take away all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then care for it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and treat it carefully, because as long as the bone is corrupted there, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the two bones become corrupted, cut it in one as we have said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healthy.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is broken, and bruised, and it causes great pain, then you must first heal it;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the bone with a spatula-shaped instrument by cutting across from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	And guard that the blade does not come until the flesh which is below the bone, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, place something above it which soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the sore does from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two joints which are born in the hands of some men by chance are entirely fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is sometimes bone, and sometimes there is a nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in no one's two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born in no one's two does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and he who is born at the joint of the two, by chance moves.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The waist of one who is fleshy is light, in such manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint, is grievous to cure; so keep it from being cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or should be at the end of the buttock, you should first cut away the rounded flesh until the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then set the bone to a suitable cloth for that, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The seams that come to two together come by birth, or by soldering of a wound, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary that you set that seam so that the parts return according to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or cloths softened in rose oil so they do not close.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	And you put between two pieces of fine lead, until their edges are soldered, as it is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If soldering comes to none of its two with the palm, then that soldering as it is fitting.
Des vils	Of vil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are thick and full of melancholy superfluities, that come in more members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more happens in legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, than to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer to him once purging of colocynth, and then the herb from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure with iron is done in two ways: one is with the cauterization, and then drawing out black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you open the vein and draw all of the blood from it.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The hip is treated in this manner: first, raise the leg in hot water very strongly, until the large sinew becomes thin.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then restrain the leg of the patient from above the hip down to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut open a vein in one place, or in two or in three, of a wide size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then draw and pour out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much sinew as the strength of the patient can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then the bandage, and command him to stay on a diet of meats avoiding black cabbage.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and restart evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevation of the leg of the patient is according to this manner: raise the leg of the patient if there is a lot of hair.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and rise the leg with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, then warm it by the fire, and then place it in the vein between the ankle and the knee, or below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then work the skin with the incision, and scrape the vein from each side until it appears when felt.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the point below, until it is raised from the skin, and then lean it on the incision lightly,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then the cut in one other place above three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then lift the vein to its root, as you have done, and bend it onto another needle, as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then cut another notch, or more if you need them, then lift the vein, and cut at the two points of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then pull and lift it up to the second notch; then extract it notch by notch until all of it comes out, then cut.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, then put a needle to the whole. that is, a strong double thread
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it and draw it out, and put below that one (thread), and turn your hand this way and that, until it comes out
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and keep it from breaking, for if it breaks, then one cannot draw it out nor lift it, and there comes annoyance to the patient
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drawn it out completely, place over the wound's spot wool moistened in wine and rose oil; and care for it until it is healed
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	if it is necessary that you cut it tortuously, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut, so that it only cuts the vein
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of a large curve, because if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the form:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees are born, and in land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it is born elsewhere than in legs, and this happens due to rot that comes from under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	just as it comes from within the body of serpents and worms, lodged between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then it changes its color, and begins the vein to pour out, as like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head opens, then it is necessary that you enclose around a piece of plank from one and a half to two finger-widths, and the knot,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the plank on the leg, and all times that it is in pain at the outside, then envelop around the plank, and the knot;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remaining portion, and do not cut it at its root, until it is fully out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it enters into the flesh, and brings about abscess and rot there, and bad sickness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore, for that reason, it is necessary that it be treated piece by piece until the top, and nothing of it remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein when it is treated of five palms long, or of ten,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	And one man came to me, who had it [an ailment] that was ten palms in length, and when you cut it, it shoots out one ray or spur, and it pierces right through to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	So that all of it issues; and be emptied the matter that is inside, and administer to the place medicines preventing corruption any day, then heal it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And at this vein some pains, and also when it opens in the joint of the foot, or foot,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and from it much spurts, and from which it shoots pains; cure it therefore as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land “ox disease,” because it often happens to oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and one feels it well at the alert of limb to limb, until they reach the skin where it goes, and leaps further;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by rot from some humors, like those that come towards snakes and worms and parasites in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubt is cast upon its malice, for when it travels through the body and goes up to the head and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	perhaps it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and drained, one can only help when it goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so then it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong bandage tightly
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cover it and treat the wound, and if the bone is embedded in the flesh and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire until it dries.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it inflames the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming or near the eye, restrain below him the eyebrow form, then cut above, and the drive out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	And it is necessary to use the patient of purification of body of medicines dissolving for the ills humors corrupted,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if worse of meats engendering putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and .i. poc after, I saw it rise as if a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more quickly than anything, as quickly as living silver when it departs from its place.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departs from that location and moves into the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little while after it spreads throughout the body until it reaches the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was returning again around her body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I have never seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I have seen many who well had moved pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I have never seen it like this, as I see it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this appears that constraint windiness;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and swollen veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see curing this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the lesion above and below evenly, and then cut as much as that constraint windiness at its place has been removed;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure of those who release wind, such as foul pills, and pills of safflower, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that some have large points, and small ones, and hairy ones, and smooth ones.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those which have parts;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and those that fall in any member so they fall in two ways: or in the principal member it falls,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, stomach, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she falls therefore into any place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I shall tell you after, appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary that you take care of the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in many circumstances;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not embedded deeply, then treat it, and care for the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps the dura mater which is on the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when scotome and sod and eversion and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and mixing of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps this without force from the nostrils, or ears; and perhaps loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jump from the wound moisture white resembling to poultices, and in jump also as burned of flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then hold off from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not within.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were fixed in a hard thing, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the seventh moves also like the pulse, and in short black blood, and comes coldness and sweat cold, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Know then without doubt that death descends.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the little arrow that does not come out is that without pains of foam leaps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and sighs loudly and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the shoulder, it is near the ribs; and it gives great pain and great suffering and sighing; and it moves all the members from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps some undigested food will jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and nothing of straw comes out through the intestines, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
