Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine comes out with it and flows, and the patient feels intense pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and necks and throat and shoulder and auxiliary and spine of the back and  forearms and hips and legs, and similar members, are saved according to more dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for this reason that you do something like that.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man with an arrow that fell or stuck in the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and drew it from another side under the fat of the ear, and was healed without any sense [of pain or problem].
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And treat with a game an arrow that falls in the fat of the eye under the skin.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was removed, and one could only reach the point towards the shaft,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, all i. with light iron without ears; the game was unharmed, and he suffered no ill consequences.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And treat an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I became the beards, and I subtly did until I betrayed it, and was healed the Christians.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And betrayed an arrow to one man, that he was in his belly, and thought that he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then that he had passed thirty days, so he did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the arrow, and I tightened it, and betrayed it further, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man whose arrow was shot into his back or belly, and the wound was closed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor causes any ailment in any of his natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, to whom an arrow was shot into his face, and the wound closed over;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remains so suffering great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And treat an arrow in  a lord, the king, that it was stuck between his eyes,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly leaning to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called in for treatment after three days had passed. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I felt it with a whole subtle tent, and I did not feel it at all.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt a prickling and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought that it was from the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on its place a plaster atractive and digestible, because the  place did not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I appeared the way of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put the bandage on it that day, and closed the wound tightly, and left the patient like that for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow inside his flesh; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a sharp corrosive medicine for several days, until it was open
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	And feel it, and feel the head of the arrow that is straightening to its place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I adjusted it in the opening of the wound with that sharp medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	And it pierced well through its ends for about four months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And then I widened the wound so that I put the forceps in it, and my hand on one side and on the other, and it could not move out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Therefore do not cease to subtly work and devise ways of instruments, until I took one day a very well-made pair of pliers
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I treated it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the mirrors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was healed entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or you have been told the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your care on those which I do not say, because the books cannot fully comprehend them all;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters learn well from a little thing, and from those that are present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new works, and nine instruments, to the understanding of strange things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are not from members where they are fixed otherwise than according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which leaps further than where it enters, is an arrow entering the flesh, and leaping never again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not leap now, then let it remain until the flesh is healed inside, and the exit be cleaned;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is fixed to the bone, and it cannot be removed, leave it so for some days, and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump, and if it does not jump, pierce around it to all i.e., forest subtle, until the ligaments around are enlarged, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: then do not treat it, but leave it so until it is healed after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes as far as the shaft, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come as far as the shaft,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for several days without ill consequence, then the engine of healing.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply stuck and cannot be drawn out further, then administer the aforementioned poultice, as I have told you; then cure the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is put back into its place in the body, if it cannot be seen, then try to bring it out completely.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then pull it out with no suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot do so because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow.
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there are no bones or nerves or veins, then widen it as much as the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears in the arrowhead to what it holds
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if bone is stuck which is embedded in two parts as much as you can
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as much as you can pull it out
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and subtly so that you do not break the arrow, but that you pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then put it back into its place until the pain is reduced, then treat it, because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood goes against you, then administer what we have said about its treatment in this chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard yourself from the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put every effort you can to safely remove the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	whether quickly or slowly, whether firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form in which he was when the arrow struck him,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, or where one sees or feels nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in that place:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then there, as long as the pincers can take hold, and then extract it; if it leaps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be drawn out, leave it there still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if the shaft of the arrow is in there, take out the whole shaft.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if the shaft has fallen, and you see administering a push is helpful, administer one instrument's thrust.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	So that the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument; and then push it out.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is embedded, put one instrument with a pointed tip into it, to help in the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is encircled, then it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it should be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow strikes in the thigh or abdomen or bladder or ribs, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut into it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and guard yourself from cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary is.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and take care of it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows are similar to the beak of an eye, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the end of a hair is like the feather of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	To put at the tip of an arrow, as its shape is:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of pliers to put in and to know if it is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of veins from which one heals are thirty-one, from which it has or head sixteen.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	That is to say: two veins that are after the ears, which are called the two "herbech";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in two temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the nose
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two veins which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the upper lip above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly used are five in each arm.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic, and it is on the inner side of the arm, and the common people call it “vein of the head.”
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called "bastard", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the outer side
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is on the hollow.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is the one that we drain, which opens manifestly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the saphenous vein is the vein that is between the index and ring finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one of which is below the curvature of the pouch of the left rib;
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein which is in the right ankle; and the vein which is called “ness,” which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The saphenous vein that is after the ears helps with old catarrh and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the saphenous vein, as I tell you, and is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then strap the patient's neck to a vice
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two lengths depending from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	who then at your hip, and where you feel the pulse below your hip, if it is feeling;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and thrust it below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein above,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and the skin and vein well two times through, and make blood issue as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then restrain and bind it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The draining of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is good for old migraines,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and suddenly, and habitual ophthalmia, and to the body of tears sharp to the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the blood are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient stretches his neck so that the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and he feels the pulse beneath his right ear and then judges it in terms of;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then gently raise the vein with your right index finger and push the lancet under.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein upwards, and cover it, just as you have done with the other two veins, and draw blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then unbind the patient, and put your right hand over the vein for an hour, then place cotton on top;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then form a bandage, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken about their covering and extraction, as the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bloodletting of the vein on the forehead is as valuable as the bloodletting of the cephalic for diseases of the face, headaches, and vertigo.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the quality of this is that the patient strains their neck by twisting, until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called "fousseur", whose form is here:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then bind the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and never again work with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not proper that the flames be too thick; and heal across because the bone is close, and perhaps break the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in two tear ducts helps the eyes, and to the forehead, and to the cheek, and to the edge around the eye, and to diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their healing are that the patient strains his neck by twisting with some rope, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then heal it, and let the healing be through the skin, a little through the long, a little wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps it breaks; then make a correction with blood, as much as you need, and then tie it on cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The vein's healing is good for fever, and for sudden pain, and for facial illnesses,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, and even when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the qualities of the vein are such that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his chin to your left hand
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a fine subtle flame, and put it between the lips in the space which is between the two nostrils
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well in this way, and the blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too far in its depth, and make it bleed according to your need, then tie it up at night, for it is very quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the two guindeges helps in the treatment of the eye, and at the beginning of the measles, and many diseases, and inflammation, and corrosion, and herpes, and scabies.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the qualities of the blood are that the sick person pulls out his neck under one and the other, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing above the head of the sick person, and the sick person sit on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then heal the vein well long a little widely, then draw blood moderately, or as much is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then redo the other side in the other vein, then untie the linen, and hold all the veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient doesn't strangle; and leave it until morning so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of healing the books
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting of veins of the lips above helps in the ulcer in the mouth, and the corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and sores and ulcers.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of bloodletting are to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you know them by that they are black, and by that around them veins small black;
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	therefore take both, and if you do not know them, and you are doubtful.
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if take the larger of each side, and also make two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the vein beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The vein beneath the tongue helps after the cephalic vein, and it is for the stricture of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the veins are that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lift the tongue, and look under on each side a vein black:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	so feel one and the other, and do not go too deep, because under are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm which commonly are bled are felt according to two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or they are pricked at all  1. a single flame martin wide, or olive subtle as you cut trenches, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very renowned, and is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary for opening the prominent veins filled with thick, apparent blood, and that contain thick and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive-shaped flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle pointed, and is for healing veins subtly, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps in diseases that are under the throat, and neck, and breast, and belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the healer to heal wisely, and that he warns himself of the artery which is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and bleeding comes forth, then it befits him to stanch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame must not prick, but cut like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then you should restrain it, and change another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want no vein of it, or you open in its place the vein in the arm; it opens manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cup to the knife-like flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see to know the place of the sinew, then it is fitting so that you extract the arm, that you touch the place until you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the place of the incision, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the flame Anesilic;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and guard that you do not wound in the artery when you see the place inflamed, because it is of the artery: avoid therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rise up high as well as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood of the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and put your leg on a length of cloth, then pull your leg up if it has not been pulled, which happens many times.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Bind his arm, and let him so remain, and do not move it the patient; and be in fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if his arm is not set straight, and he feels pain, and the medicine is not present, then tie off the artery if it opens up, because the head of the retraction; and set the arm straight.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fig bark, and make it soft, and take one half and bind it well until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the bleeding is stopped, it is well; if it is not, then treat it, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of the bleeding is not always achieved in many cases because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The blood from the vein in the middle helps treat blood from the head above, and from the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the physician to feel with his hand over the nerve that is beneath, and if they are not too much inflamed, and he feels the nerve
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and he inflates it and the saintes be grieved, and by chance cannot heal
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any men because of its subtlety, then it is necessary that you feel it with the instrument anesthetized; and push the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision along the length
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bloodletting of the cephalic vein so aids, that it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is proper to bleed by pricking at the olive vein or the myrtle vein, because it is the safest of all veins, because it has neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is proper to seek the lighter spot, and do not worry if one fails the first time, and you begin again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance, it swells for some men when one tries the first time, but it does not matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The qualities of the vein are according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing that you must know about bloodletting is that it is only administered for the sake of preserving health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to ward off diseases to come;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and that the bloodletting be done in one of the three veins which are known as cephalic, femoral, and basilica;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one must bloodletting at the beginning of Lent, and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And one must bloodletting on the first day or the third, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	Bloodletting which is administered to illnesses has no determined hour, but when need is of day or of night, at all hours and in all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it does not behoove to bloodlet children until fourteen years old, nor women carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not bleed the old man who has passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they cleanse the bowels with a light enema,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has much phlegm retained, so that the veins do not draw the superfluous and harmful excretions from the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	do not bleed those who are too full of meat, nor those who are drunk, until they are sober, nor those with dropsy;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if one warse on after colic passion, and vomiting, and swelling of the belly, and multiplication of labor in woman, and of travail, of wakefulness and of fasting, and that which all virtue, or by thing of the weapon or of the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtlety the humors, if they are thick, by meats and by drinks and by medicines, if you have their power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter into a bath, if nothing forbids it, to subtlety the blood;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal the vein of the pit entrails as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And guard yourself from work, and from pricking, and from lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And be bound and joined, and let the hand of the one who is healing be higher than the one being healed, and rub the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then stretch the ligament in the middle, for when it is too stretched or pulled, it cannot be corrected properly.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the place with your hands, until the veins swell up and are felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the vein with a drop of old oil, then put his finger of his left hand on that vein under its location a little bit where he wants to open
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein is not cut and made with iron.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that are as thick as cords to open, and some that are full of windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts the cautery on it, it retracts from the cautery, and cannot open the vein, and this is how it happens with those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he works on the vein, if the wound is too tight, for this it is necessary that the surgeons be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is worked on the first time, it is good; if not, he begins again a little below where it was, if the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the veins are inflamed, and the patient is afraid, then he leaves it for one or two days, and does not bind up the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	for perchance abscesses will come; nor enter into a bath, then he begins again the bleeding if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the vein short and you doubt that it will not give as much blood as you see, then pierce in that same opening all the way directly;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and make a little incision, so that the edges are swollen; because this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, do not begin the bloodletting again, and put a little olive oil on it, because it heals the body from blood, and is better in this case than any other ointment.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer olive oil in every bloodletting that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and that same action is tripled and bowed of them, when one puts it in its place; so subtle the sinews are and they part when it is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes to it an abscess large, which happens often, even when it is drained only that time when the opening of the vein is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you hurry, and put on it a sponge moistened in water and some heat, and hold it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is proper that you do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after several days without any blackness or greenness, then it does not harm it.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, put on no thing of aloes or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, mint, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearance to the basilica's  health: put therefore your hand on, and if you find the place soft at the pressure of the hand, so is that appearance evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore that you put on anything of those we have said, for by chance it may lack the artery; but let him I bandage I plaster dry to harden the place, then its care other care, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each one with blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it ooze until it is red; and if you see it swollen, let it subside until it is smaller; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for one who is weak and frail, and needs the extraction of blood, let a wider wound be made, and the flames be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for one who is feeble, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed them often and little, and you must bleed them by cutting across, not pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bleeding is safe from the loss of blood and severance of nerves, and is more useful than bleeding deeply or widely.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to the one whose body needs bloodletting, it is fitting to give softened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is feverish, treat with blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexion,  soak bread in syrup of figs, or in a syrup of aromatic honey with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he faints during bloodletting, after the exit of a mouthful of blood, it is fitting that he suck broth of meat and subtle aromatic syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to empty his arm, and bleed other times, if it is needed, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to empty his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed from another part, he must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because he has much blood inside the body that is already exhausted, and brings fever; so in this case, it is necessary to draw a large quantity, and widen the opening until it drips in pellets.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	since you are aware of all the conditions of health, and place your hand upon his pulse when it is healthy, that death may not come in place of the pains
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not behoove you when you see the arm dislocated, and make blood flow a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press firmly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	and if it is curved, that he extend the arm completely, for that would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it be until it heals the second time; or you point it to the tip of the flame, as long as the vein that is frozen should not be pierced from the vein.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on i. pock of oil re-applied, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not constrict it at all, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood a second time, let it be done in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled in the place of the vein in the neck because it is composed there.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient puts their hand in hot water until the bones are red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then be bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then bleed now through the middle, neither wide nor long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and be the puncture wide, and bleed well near the joint of the hand, and if without it can issue, then put the hand back into hot water, and leave the blood in the water, until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in this state, do not put the hand in hot water, because one puts it in more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this chapter is safer from all other veins, because there is neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the salvation of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strait the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, if one sees it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the bone is broken crookedly, and if you cut it straight through entirely, it will not cause any harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not push it too far in, because the nerves are all exposed bare of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water, if it has become numb in the wound, and cannot be moved.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, then put oil and wool on top of the vein to keep it covered tightly, and do this for each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sinew of the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The sinew of the sophene is good for all the diseases that are below the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	as many as diseases of the joints, and retention of flowers, and illness of the hips, and thighs and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of this sinew are that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs on the vein until it warms.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and bind above the ankle joint; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	so take then the larger vein, or at the ankle, which seems best.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut it above the foot, guard the nerves which are below, and cut in a way similar to when cutting into [something]; and let the flame be annealed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot flow out, put the foot back in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is necessary to cut the wound a first time, then begin again above a bit, because the blood flow is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and then do the same thing from the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of the foot, and its bleeding is good for the pain in the hip, when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of its bleeding are that the patient enters a bath and is restrained above the ankle four fingers in twisting
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then close it in all ways that you can, and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, for the veins are dry, and it is well supplied with blood by the hands of men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then close any vein that opens or on the back of the foot, and towards the lower part, and guard against the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make as much blood flow as you see, and then untie the bandage, and put on cotton and restrain it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of leeching
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made of horns, or glass, or wood; and leeching is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this leeching which is without piercing is done in two ways: either it is hot, or cold;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and leeching which is done by piercing and drawing blood is done in fourteen places on the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is entirely in the neck; and the other is in the collar.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in two ribs of the neck; and the windpipe below the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the windpipe at the two shoulders; and the windpipe above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the windpipes in the two arms; and the windpipes of the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction cups on the two ankles; and the suction does not treat blood, except for the small veins that are scattered in the flesh
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore it does not weaken them as much, as one does with a vein-letting.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not suitable to be administered, neither with hot nor cold fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of disease it is necessary to use suction cups, or out of custom, then we administer them every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and midway, and at any time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they need to blow, have heavy head
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and they have those who experience bloating and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness around their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and bleed from the gums;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see through blood-red mist and corpses and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is removed after.iii. hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bloodletting of the temple helps in the great pain of the head... which comes to the eyes, and it is not right that it should be done after the evacuation of the whole body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventousation is in place of the bloodletting of the cephalic.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not right that those who are of cold complexion should use it, or those who have diarrhea, because this does great harm to them;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it is not suitable for the elderly to use, nor those who have or are afflicted with cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal from it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Cupping on the neck is in place of the cure of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is useful to the extraction of phlegm.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to the opening of the channel of the throat, and to all other ailments, and to congestion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and there it is fitting not to press too hard, for if it holds too tightly, it can cause obstruction in the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventilations of the two ribs of the neck are good for pains in the head, and headache, and migraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in the place of the vein of the basilica; and it is fitting that you command the patient to spread his hand when putting it, that he does not cut the artery, and does not bring a discharge of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventilations below the chin are good for mouth disease, and gum rot, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for illness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventilation of the armpits is as good as three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instructs the patient not to let too much be worn upon it, for its skin is bare of flesh and shows beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup which is on the haunches is good for hemorrhoids of the foundation, and for diseases below, and it should be large, and of iron, that it has need to well draw; and perhaps if it were thin, it would break; and in this way it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups of the legs are applied openly, because they attract blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the hips, and of the thighs, and of the bladder, and soften the tumors; and they are placed in the place of the two calves, and of the two ankles, but nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and succeed temperately, and place it firmly, and move it equally, and do not cease to do this, until you see the place red and inflamed, and appear the color of blood; then firm, and replace the suction cups, and take care in the disposition of the body, because there are such who have tender flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to pierce it twice: the first time to thin the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to pierce it a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we repeat often; and if the vein is thick, pierce it in depth, and the end is that the cords be pierced soundly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it behoves him who has thick and hard skin, and who has large pores, that you anoint the places of the cupping glasses with oil appetizing and dissolving.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in this state, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of pumpkin seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the ear, of watercress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, then take bitter oil, or balm, or dill seed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one whom you are treating has tender flesh and wide pores, then it is not necessary to put any oil there;
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash after the suction of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or gourd water, or china water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them rise from rosemary water, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluities, they rise from old wine, or buckthorn water, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to apply cupping before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and do not sleep after cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary for him to worsen when he must be winded and when he is winded.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are healed and are choleric, and if their flesh is too much aggravated and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary for them to eat cold things, such as pomegranates and chicory and lettuce at the waist, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and minced beans, and boar meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, so take syrup of honey and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and quince, and quince seeds and small onions and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day that he will feel better, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give no man at any time thyme or nutmeg before or after the opening of a vein, in order to comfort the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let it be subtle [prepared] the wine, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The suction cups that are put on without hurting are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the chest and the hips and the hip, because these members do not suffer being hurt on them.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one does it only in order to draw blood from limb to limb.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we put on the breasts when the milk comes in; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we put suction cups on the belly and chest to lessen the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain when there is an obstruction or stone, as it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And thus it is done when one puts it on the liver and on the mouse when there is retained wind.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these suction cups are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with tepid water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in diseases of the lungs, and in this manner one fills the suction cup with hot water only, or with water in which herbs suitable to it have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And have two boards of width and half a palm length, and have or costate around the middle one small hole, as for putting in a needle
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And let it be of wood, soft facing so that it does not burn the patient when putting it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And have in the middle a crossbar of wood or iron, to put a candle enclosed,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let them be both large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the cupping glasses of children are other than those of old people, and of the thin ones than of the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And should one thus place this cupping glass upon the limb?
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take the candle of wax or .i. ointment, and place it within the cupping glass opposite the rod which is within the cupping glass,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light be at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it upon the limb, and these must be upon the opening that we have said, so that when one wants to, air goes in there, and one removes the suction cup.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and grasp the linen as before, and repeat it often, if you have need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup which is administered in the illness of pleurisy, on no occasion has it a rod or opening, and is not administered except when it is full of air, and is placed upon the limb only for a while.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suctions are brought only to limbs where one cannot put suction cups because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar things;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in their naked flesh, such as the two or three, and similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the qualities of the user are that when you find suctions that are in clear fresh waters without impurities, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in fresh water until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then let it be cleaned by leech and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the bandages.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flat, and will fall, if it is their place where one can put a cupping, then put it, because it helps a lot afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If those are not there, lift the place with ease, then with water, very well, and then bind it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the sores heal too much after the bandages of the skin, then moisten 1 linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the bandage is softened.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wounds are multiplied, put on top pounded vitriol, or salt, and similar things, until they are stretched.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on top half of peeled beans, and let them stay there until they dry out on the spot, then it will stop.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the bandages do not want to be taken, rub the spot with fresh blood, or insert a needle there until the bandages loosen.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them above, and as soon as they feel the blood, they burn;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are bleeding, sprinkle on a little powder of aloes and silk ground together, or ashes, they will now stop burning.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear child, that the fools who read from this chapter will never see anything in any of the old books, nor will they ever read a letter from them.
